{"type":"user","message":{"role":"user","content":[{"tool_use_id":"toolu_017HuazgQfH5R63Cg89jWFpp","type":"tool_result","content":"{\"content\":\"1: We welcome contributions from the community. Please read the following guidelines carefully to\\n2: maximize the chances of your PR being merged.\\n3: \\n4: # Communication\\n5: \\n6: * Before starting work on a major feature, please reach out to us via GitHub, Slack,\\n7:   email, etc. We will make sure no one else is already working on it and ask you to open a\\n8:   GitHub issue.\\n9: * A \\\"major feature\\\" is defined as any change that is > 100 LOC altered (not including tests), or\\n10:   changes any user-facing behavior. We will use the GitHub issue to discuss the feature and come to\\n11:   agreement. This is to prevent your time being wasted, as well as ours. The GitHub review process\\n12:   for major features is also important so that [organizations with commit access](OWNERS.md) can\\n13:   come to agreement on design. If it is appropriate to write a design document, the document must\\n14:   be hosted either in the GitHub tracking issue, or linked to from the issue and hosted in a\\n15:   world-readable location.\\n16: * Specifically, if the goal is to add a new [extension](REPO_LAYOUT.md#sourceextensions-layout),\\n17:   please read the [extension policy](GOVERNANCE.md#extension-addition-policy).\\n18: * Small patches and bug fixes don't need prior communication.\\n19: \\n20: # Coding style\\n21: \\n22: * See [STYLE.md](STYLE.md)\\n23: \\n24: # Inclusive language policy\\n25: \\n26: The Envoy community has an explicit goal to be inclusive to all. As such, all PRs must adhere to the\\n27: following guidelines for all code, APIs, and documentation:\\n28: \\n29: * The following words and phrases are not allowed:\\n30:   * *Whitelist*: use allowlist instead.\\n31:   * *Blacklist*: use denylist or blocklist instead.\\n32:   * *Master*: use primary or main instead.\\n33:   * *Slave*: use secondary or replica instead.\\n34: * Documentation should be written in an inclusive style. The [Google developer\\n35:   documentation](https://developers.google.com/style/inclusive-documentation) contains an excellent\\n36:   reference on this topic.\\n37: * The above policy is not considered definitive and may be amended in the future as industry best\\n38:   practices evolve. Additional comments on this topic may be provided by maintainers during code\\n39:   review.\\n40: \\n41: # Breaking change policy\\n42: \\n43: Both API and implementation stability are important to Envoy. Since the API is consumed by clients\\n44: beyond Envoy, it has a distinct set of [versioning guidelines](api/API_VERSIONING.md). Below, we\\n45: articulate the Envoy implementation stability rules, which operate within the context of the API\\n46: versioning guidelines:\\n47: \\n48: * Features may be marked as deprecated in a given versioned API at any point in time, but this may\\n49:   only be done when a replacement implementation and configuration path is available in Envoy on\\n50:   main. Deprecators must implement a conversion from the deprecated configuration to the latest\\n51:   `vNalpha` (with the deprecated field) that Envoy uses internally. A field may be deprecated if\\n52:   this tool would be able to perform the conversion. For example, removing a field to describe\\n53:   HTTP/2 window settings is valid if a more comprehensive HTTP/2 protocol options field is being\\n54:   introduced to replace it. The PR author deprecating the old configuration is responsible for\\n55:   updating all tests and canonical configuration, or guarding them with the\\n56:   `DEPRECATED_FEATURE_TEST()` macro. This will be validated by the `bazel.compile_time_options`\\n57:   target, which will hard-fail when deprecated configuration is used. The majority of tests and\\n58:   configuration for a feature should be expressed in terms of the latest Envoy internal\\n59:   configuration (i.e. `vNalpha`), only a minimal number of tests necessary to validate configuration\\n60:   translation should be guarded via the `DEPRECATED_FEATURE_TEST()` macro.\\n61: * We will delete deprecated configuration across major API versions. E.g. a field marked deprecated\\n62:   in v2 will be removed in v3.\\n63: * Unless the community and Envoy maintainer team agrees on an exception, during the\\n64:   first release cycle after a feature has been deprecated, use of that feature\\n65:   will cause a logged warning, and incrementing the\\n66:   [runtime](https://www.envoyproxy.io/docs/envoy/latest/configuration/operations/runtime#statistics)\\n67:   `runtime.deprecated_feature_use` stat.\\n68:   During the second release cycle, use of the deprecated configuration will\\n69:   cause a configuration load failure, unless the feature in question is\\n70:   explicitly overridden in\\n71:   [runtime](https://www.envoyproxy.io/docs/envoy/latest/configuration/operations/runtime#using-runtime-overrides-for-deprecated-features)\\n72:   config ([example](configs/using_deprecated_config.yaml)), or if\\n73:   `envoy.features.enable_all_deprecated_features` is set to true. Finally, following the deprecation\\n74:   of the API major version where the field was first marked deprecated, the entire implementation\\n75:   code will be removed from the Envoy implementation.\\n76: * If the runtime key `envoy.features.fail_on_any_deprecated_feature` is enabled,\\n77:   use of deprecated fields will trigger a configuration load failure\\n78:   rather than a logged warning.\\n79: * This policy means that organizations deploying main should have some time to get ready for\\n80:   breaking changes at the next major API version. This is typically a window of at least 12 months\\n81:   or until the organization moves to the next major API version.\\n82: * The breaking change policy also applies to source level extensions (e.g., filters). Code that\\n83:   conforms to the public interface documentation should continue to compile and work within the\\n84:   deprecation window. Within this window, a warning of deprecation should be carefully logged (some\\n85:   features might need rate limiting for logging this). We make no guarantees about code or deployments\\n86:   that rely on undocumented behavior. See [extension removal policy](./EXTENSION_POLICY.md#removing-existing-extensions)\\n87:   for more information.\\n88: * All deprecations/breaking changes will be clearly listed in the [version history](docs/root/version_history/).\\n89: * High risk deprecations/breaking changes may be announced to the\\n90:   [envoy-announce](https://groups.google.com/forum/#!forum/envoy-announce) email list but by default\\n91:   it is expected the multi-phase warn-by-default/fail-by-default is sufficient to warn users to move\\n92:   away from deprecated features.\\n93: \\n94: # Submitting a PR\\n95: \\n96: * Fork the repo.\\n97: * In your local repo, install the git hooks that implement various important pre-commit and\\n98:   pre-push checks:\\n99: \\n100:   ```\\n101:   ./support/bootstrap\\n102:   ```\\n103: \\n104:   Please see [support/README.md](support/README.md) for more information on these hooks.\\n105: \\n106: * Create your PR. If your PR adds new code, it should include tests [covering](source/docs/coverage.md) the new code. Please note that draft PRs may not be reviewed and will likely not be triaged, so do not create your PR as a draft if you want prompt reviews!\\n107: * Tests will automatically run for you.\\n108: * We will **not** merge any PR that is not passing tests.\\n109: * PRs are expected to have 100% test coverage for added code. This can be verified with a coverage\\n110:   build. If your PR cannot have 100% coverage for some reason please clearly explain why when you\\n111:   open it.\\n112: * Any PR that changes user-facing behavior **must** have associated documentation in [docs](docs) as\\n113:   well as [release notes](changelogs/current.yaml). API changes should be documented\\n114:   inline with protos as per the [API contribution guidelines](api/CONTRIBUTING.md). If a change applies\\n115:   to multiple sections of the release notes, it should be noted in the first (most important) section\\n116:   that applies. For instance, a bug fix that introduces incompatible behavior should be noted in\\n117:   `Incompatible Behavior Changes` but not in `Bug Fixes`.\\n118: * All code comments and documentation are expected to have proper English grammar and punctuation.\\n119:   If you are not a fluent English speaker (or a bad writer ;-)) please let us know and we will try\\n120:   to find some help but there are no guarantees.\\n121: * Your PR title should be descriptive, and generally start with a subsystem name followed by a\\n122:   colon. Examples:\\n123:   * \\\"docs: fix grammar error\\\"\\n124:   * \\\"http conn man: add new feature\\\"\\n125: * Your PR commit message will be used as the commit message when your PR is merged. You should\\n126:   update this field if your PR diverges during review.\\n127: * Your PR description should have details on what the PR does. If it fixes an existing issue it\\n128:   should end with \\\"Fixes #XXX\\\".\\n129: * If your PR is co-authored or based on an earlier PR from another contributor,\\n130:   please attribute them with `Co-authored-by: name <name@example.com>`. See\\n131:   GitHub's [multiple author\\n132:   guidance](https://help.github.com/en/github/committing-changes-to-your-project/creating-a-commit-with-multiple-authors)\\n133:   for further details.\\n134: * When all of the tests are passing and all other conditions described herein are satisfied, a\\n135:   maintainer will be assigned to review and merge the PR.\\n136: * Once your PR is under review, *please do not rebase it*. If you rebase, you will need to force push to\\n137:   github, and github's user interface will force your reviewer to review the PR\\n138:   from scratch rather than simply look at your latest changes.  It's much easier to review\\n139:   new commits and/or merges. We squash rebase the final merged commit so the number of commits\\n140:   you have in the PR don't matter. Again once your PR is assigned a reviewer, unless you need to fix DCO\\n141:   *please do not force push*.  If you need to pull recent changes you can run\\n142:   ```\\n143:   branch=$(git status|head -1|cut -f3 -d\\\\ )\\n144:   git checkout main\\n145:   git pull\\n146:   git checkout \\\"$branch\\\"\\n147:   git merge main\\n148:   ```\\n149: * We expect that once a PR is opened, it will be actively worked on until it is merged or closed.\\n150:   We reserve the right to close PRs that are not making progress. This is generally defined as no\\n151:   changes for 7 days. Obviously PRs that are closed due to lack of activity can be reopened later.\\n152:   Closing stale PRs helps us to keep on top of all of the work currently in flight.\\n153: * If a commit deprecates a feature, the commit message must mention what has been deprecated.\\n154:   Additionally, the [version history](changelogs/current.yaml) must be updated with\\n155:   relevant RST links for fields and messages as part of the commit.\\n156: * Please consider joining the [envoy-dev](https://groups.google.com/forum/#!forum/envoy-dev)\\n157:   mailing list.\\n158: * If your PR involves any changes to\\n159:   [envoy-filter-example](https://github.com/envoyproxy/envoy-filter-example) (for example making a new\\n160:   branch so that CI can pass) it is your responsibility to follow through with merging those\\n161:   changes back to main once the CI dance is done.\\n162: * If your PR is a high risk change, the reviewer may ask that you runtime guard\\n163:   it. See the section on runtime guarding below.\\n164: \\n165: \\n166: # Runtime guarding\\n167: \\n168: Some changes in Envoy are deemed worthy of runtime guarding. Instead of just replacing\\n169: old code with new code, both code paths are supported for between one Envoy release (if it is\\n170: guarded due to performance concerns) and a full deprecation cycle (if it is a high risk behavioral\\n171: change). Generally as a community we try to guard both high risk changes (major\\n172: refactors such as replacing Envoy's buffer implementation) and most user-visible\\n173: non-config-guarded changes to protocol processing (for example additions or changes to HTTP headers or\\n174: how HTTP is serialized out) for non-alpha features. Feel free to tag @envoyproxy/maintainers\\n175: if you aren't sure if a given change merits runtime guarding.\\n176: \\n177: The canonical way to runtime guard a feature is\\n178: ```\\n179: if (Runtime::runtimeFeatureEnabled(\\\"envoy.reloadable_features.my_feature_name\\\")) {\\n180:   [new code path]\\n181: } else {\\n182:   [old_code_path]\\n183: }\\n184: ```\\n185: Runtime guarded features named with the \\\"envoy.reloadable_features.\\\" prefix must be safe to flip\\n186: true or false on running Envoy instances. In some situations it may make more sense to\\n187: latch the value in a member variable on class creation, for example:\\n188: \\n189: ```\\n190: bool use_new_code_path_ =\\n191:     Runtime::runtimeFeatureEnabled(\\\"envoy.reloadable_features.my_feature_name\\\")\\n192: ```\\n193: \\n194: This should only be done if the lifetime of the object in question is relatively short compared to\\n195: the lifetime of most Envoy instances, i.e. latching state on creation of the\\n196: Http::ConnectionManagerImpl or all Network::ConnectionImpl classes, to ensure that the new behavior\\n197: will be exercised as the runtime value is flipped, and that the old behavior will trail off over\\n198: time.\\n199: \\n200: Runtime guarded features may either set true (running the new code by default) in the initial PR,\\n201: after a testing interval, or during the next release cycle, at the PR author's and reviewing\\n202: maintainer's discretion. Generally all runtime guarded features will be set true when a\\n203: release is cut. Old code paths for refactors can be cleaned up after a release and there has been\\n204: some production run time. Old code for behavioral changes will be deprecated after six months if no\\n205: Envoy operators have raised concerns. If the behavioral change is problematic for any Envoy users,\\n206: the maintainers team will work to find a satisfactory resolution, generally in the form of a permanent\\n207: configuration knob for the behavioral differences.\\n208: \\n209: Runtime features are set true by default by inclusion in\\n210: [source/common/runtime/runtime_features.cc](https://github.com/envoyproxy/envoy/blob/main/source/common/runtime/runtime_features.cc)\\n211: \\n212: There are four suggested options for testing new runtime features:\\n213: \\n214: 1. Create a per-test Runtime::LoaderSingleton as done in [DeprecatedFieldsTest.IndividualFieldDisallowedWithRuntimeOverride](https://github.com/envoyproxy/envoy/blob/main/test/common/protobuf/utility_test.cc)\\n215: 2. Create a [parameterized test](https://github.com/google/googletest/blob/master/docs/advanced.md#how-to-write-value-parameterized-tests)\\n216:    where the set up of the test sets the new runtime value explicitly to\\n217:    GetParam() as outlined in (1).\\n218: 3. Set up integration tests with custom runtime defaults as documented in the\\n219:    [integration test README](https://github.com/envoyproxy/envoy/blob/main/test/integration/README.md)\\n220: 4. Run a given unit test with the new runtime value explicitly set true or false as done\\n221:    for [runtime_flag_override_test](https://github.com/envoyproxy/envoy/blob/main/test/common/runtime/BUILD)\\n222: \\n223: Runtime code is held to the same standard as regular Envoy code, so both the old\\n224: path and the new should have 100% coverage both with the feature defaulting true\\n225: and false.\\n226: \\n227: Please note that if adding a runtime guarded feature, your [release notes](changelogs/current.yaml) should include both the functional change, and how to revert it, for example\\n228: \\n229: ```yaml\\n230: - area: config\\n231:   change: |\\n232:       type URL is used to lookup extensions regardless of the name field. This may cause problems for empty filter configurations or mis-matched protobuf as the typed configurations. This behavioral change can be temporarily reverted by setting runtime guard ``envoy.reloadable_features.no_extension_lookup_by_name`` to false.\\n233: ```\\n234: \\n235: # PR review policy for maintainers\\n236: \\n237: * Typically we try to turn around reviews within one business day.\\n238: * See [OWNERS.md](OWNERS.md) for the current list of maintainers.\\n239: * It is generally expected that a senior maintainer should review every PR to\\n240:   core code. Changes which only touch tests, extensions, tools, docs or comments\\n241:   need only be reviewed by a maintainer, or senior extension maintainer.\\n242: * It is also generally expected that a \\\"domain expert\\\" for the code the PR touches should review the\\n243:   PR. This person does not necessarily need to have commit access.\\n244: * For new extensions (contrib or otherwise) and features, at least one of the approvals should be *from an\\n245:   organization different from the PR author.* E.g., if Lyft authors a PR, at least one approver\\n246:   should be from an organization other than Lyft. This helps us make sure that we aren't putting\\n247:   organization specific shortcuts into the code.\\n248:   new HTTP/3 features are largely exempt from cross-company approvals as all of the\\n249:   area experts work at a single company, but HTTP/3 changes which impact general\\n250:   functionality still merit a cross-company check.\\n251: * contrib extensions do not need senior maintainer or maintainer review only contrib owner review and\\n252:   a maintainer stamp to merge.\\n253: * If there is a question on who should review a PR please discuss in Slack.\\n254: * Anyone is welcome to review any PR that they want, whether they are a maintainer or not.\\n255: * Please make sure that the PR title, commit message, and description are updated if the PR changes\\n256:   significantly during review.\\n257: * Please **clean up the title and body** before merging. By default, GitHub fills the squash merge\\n258:   title with the original title, and the commit body with every individual commit from the PR.\\n259:   The maintainer doing the merge should make sure the title follows the guidelines above and should\\n260:   overwrite the body with the original commit message from the PR (cleaning it up if necessary)\\n261:   while preserving the PR author's final DCO sign-off.\\n262: * If a PR includes a deprecation/breaking change, notification should be sent to the\\n263:   [envoy-announce](https://groups.google.com/forum/#!forum/envoy-announce) email list.\\n264: \\n265: # API changes\\n266: \\n267: If you change anything in the [api tree](https://github.com/envoyproxy/envoy/tree/main/api),\\n268: please read the [API Review\\n269: Checklist](https://github.com/envoyproxy/envoy/tree/main/api/review_checklist.md)\\n270: and make sure that your changes have addressed all of the considerations listed there.\\n271: \\n272: # Adding new extensions\\n273: \\n274: For developers adding a new extension, one can take an existing extension as the starting point.\\n275: \\n276: Extension configuration should be located in a directory structure like\\n277: `api/envoy/extensions/area/plugin/`, for example `api/envoy/extensions/access_loggers/file/`\\n278: \\n279: The code for the extension should be located under the equivalent\\n280: `source/extensions/area/plugin`, and include an *envoy_cc_extension* with the\\n281: configuration and tagged with the appropriate security posture, and an\\n282: *envoy_cc_library* with the code.\\n283: \\n284: More details on how to add a new extension API can be found [here](api/STYLE.md#adding-an-extension-configuration-to-the-api):\\n285: \\n286: # Adding contrib extensions\\n287: \\n288: See [EXTENSION_POLICY.md](EXTENSION_POLICY.md) for more information on contrib. Adding a contrib\\n289: extension mostly mirrors adding a normal extension above. Some differences are noted here:\\n290: \\n291: * API files should be added in `api/contrib/envoy/`, but the protos' namespaces should still be as\\n292:   in normal extensions (which will make file movement easier later if the extension gets promoted\\n293:   to core).\\n294: * Build config and metadata should be included in [contrib/contrib_build_config.bzl](contrib/contrib_build_config.bzl)\\n295:   and [contrib/extensions_metadata.yaml](contrib/extensions_metadata.yaml).\\n296: * An entrypoint should be added in `docs/root/api-v3/config/contrib/contrib.rst`\\n297: \\n298: # DCO: Sign your work\\n299: \\n300: Envoy ships commit hooks that allow you to auto-generate the DCO signoff line if\\n301: it doesn't exist when you run `git commit`. Simply navigate to the Envoy project\\n302: root and run:\\n303: \\n304: ```bash\\n305: ./support/bootstrap\\n306: ```\\n307: \\n308: From here, simply commit as normal, and you will see the signoff at the bottom\\n309: of each commit.\\n310: \\n311: The sign-off is a simple line at the end of the explanation for the\\n312: patch, which certifies that you wrote it or otherwise have the right to\\n313: pass it on as an open-source patch. The rules are pretty simple: if you\\n314: can certify the below (from\\n315: [developercertificate.org](https://developercertificate.org/)):\\n316: \\n317: ```\\n318: Developer Certificate of Origin\\n319: Version 1.1\\n320: \\n321: Copyright (C) 2004, 2006 The Linux Foundation and its contributors.\\n322: 660 York Street, Suite 102,\\n323: San Francisco, CA 94110 USA\\n324: \\n325: Everyone is permitted to copy and distribute verbatim copies of this\\n326: license document, but changing it is not allowed.\\n327: \\n328: \\n329: Developer's Certificate of Origin 1.1\\n330: \\n331: By making a contribution to this project, I certify that:\\n332: \\n333: (a) The contribution was created in whole or in part by me and I\\n334:     have the right to submit it under the open source license\\n335:     indicated in the file; or\\n336: \\n337: (b) The contribution is based upon previous work that, to the best\\n338:     of my knowledge, is covered under an appropriate open source\\n339:     license and I have the right under that license to submit that\\n340:     work with modifications, whether created in whole or in part\\n341:     by me, under the same open source license (unless I am\\n342:     permitted to submit under a different license), as indicated\\n343:     in the file; or\\n344: \\n345: (c) The contribution was provided directly to me by some other\\n346:     person who certified (a), (b) or (c) and I have not modified\\n347:     it.\\n348: \\n349: (d) I understand and agree that this project and the contribution\\n350:     are public and that a record of the contribution (including all\\n351:     personal information I submit with it, including my sign-off) is\\n352:     maintained indefinitely and may be redistributed consistent with\\n353:     this project or the open source license(s) involved.\\n354: ```\\n355: \\n356: then you just add a line to every git commit message:\\n357: \\n358:     Signed-off-by: Joe Smith <joe@gmail.com>\\n359: \\n360: using your real name (sorry, no pseudonyms or anonymous contributions.)\\n361: \\n362: You can add the sign off when creating the git commit via `git commit -s`.\\n363: \\n364: If you want this to be automatic you can set up some aliases:\\n365: \\n366: ```bash\\n367: git config --add alias.amend \\\"commit -s --amend\\\"\\n368: git config --add alias.c \\\"commit -s\\\"\\n369: ```\\n370: \\n371: ## Fixing DCO\\n372: \\n373: If your PR fails the DCO check, it's necessary to fix the entire commit history in the PR. Best\\n374: practice is to [squash](https://gitready.com/advanced/2009/02/10/squashing-commits-with-rebase.html)\\n375: the commit history to a single commit, append the DCO sign-off as described above, and [force\\n376: push](https://git-scm.com/docs/git-push#git-push---force). For example, if you have 2 commits in\\n377: your history:\\n378: \\n379: ```bash\\n380: git rebase -i HEAD^^\\n381: (interactive squash + DCO append)\\n382: git push origin -f\\n383: ```\\n384: \\n385: Note, that in general rewriting history in this way is a hindrance to the review process and this\\n386: should only be done to correct a DCO mistake.\\n387: \\n388: ## Triggering CI re-run without making changes\\n389: \\n390: To rerun failed tasks in Azure pipelines, add a comment with the line\\n391: \\n392: ```\\n393: /retest\\n394: ```\\n395: \\n396: in it. This should rebuild only the failed tasks.\\n397: \\n398: Sometimes tasks will be stuck in CI and won't be marked as failed, which means\\n399: the above command won't work. Should this happen, pushing an empty commit should\\n400: re-run all the CI tasks. Consider adding an alias into your `.gitconfig` file:\\n401: \\n402: ```\\n403: [alias]\\n404:     kick-ci = !\\\"git commit -s --allow-empty -m 'Kick CI' && git push\\\"\\n405: ```\\n406: \\n407: Once you add this alias you can issue the command `git kick-ci` and the PR\\n408: will be sent back for a retest.\\n409: \\n410: # Repo Etiquette\\n411: \\n412: Contributors with push-access to the Envoy project should prefer pushing changes to a personal fork,\\n413: including when creating branches for pull requests.\\n414: \\n415: This helps keep the Envoy repo as lean as possible, which can speed up cloning and synchronizing\\n416: operations for both developers and CI.\\n417: \",\"url\":\"https://sourcegraph.sourcegraph.com/github.com/sg-evals/envoy--v1.32.1@b35dd17bea856e19fc4e65fb05e68170841d3726/-/blob/CONTRIBUTING.md\"}"}]},"parent_tool_use_id":null,"session_id":"7a51d5b9-63f8-4c27-86d4-c47033ff4464","uuid":"2725fcbc-b30d-4094-915c-89c3f992f964","tool_use_result":{"content":"{\"content\":\"1: We welcome contributions from the community. Please read the following guidelines carefully to\\n2: maximize the chances of your PR being merged.\\n3: \\n4: # Communication\\n5: \\n6: * Before starting work on a major feature, please reach out to us via GitHub, Slack,\\n7:   email, etc. We will make sure no one else is already working on it and ask you to open a\\n8:   GitHub issue.\\n9: * A \\\"major feature\\\" is defined as any change that is > 100 LOC altered (not including tests), or\\n10:   changes any user-facing behavior. We will use the GitHub issue to discuss the feature and come to\\n11:   agreement. This is to prevent your time being wasted, as well as ours. The GitHub review process\\n12:   for major features is also important so that [organizations with commit access](OWNERS.md) can\\n13:   come to agreement on design. If it is appropriate to write a design document, the document must\\n14:   be hosted either in the GitHub tracking issue, or linked to from the issue and hosted in a\\n15:   world-readable location.\\n16: * Specifically, if the goal is to add a new [extension](REPO_LAYOUT.md#sourceextensions-layout),\\n17:   please read the [extension policy](GOVERNANCE.md#extension-addition-policy).\\n18: * Small patches and bug fixes don't need prior communication.\\n19: \\n20: # Coding style\\n21: \\n22: * See [STYLE.md](STYLE.md)\\n23: \\n24: # Inclusive language policy\\n25: \\n26: The Envoy community has an explicit goal to be inclusive to all. As such, all PRs must adhere to the\\n27: following guidelines for all code, APIs, and documentation:\\n28: \\n29: * The following words and phrases are not allowed:\\n30:   * *Whitelist*: use allowlist instead.\\n31:   * *Blacklist*: use denylist or blocklist instead.\\n32:   * *Master*: use primary or main instead.\\n33:   * *Slave*: use secondary or replica instead.\\n34: * Documentation should be written in an inclusive style. The [Google developer\\n35:   documentation](https://developers.google.com/style/inclusive-documentation) contains an excellent\\n36:   reference on this topic.\\n37: * The above policy is not considered definitive and may be amended in the future as industry best\\n38:   practices evolve. Additional comments on this topic may be provided by maintainers during code\\n39:   review.\\n40: \\n41: # Breaking change policy\\n42: \\n43: Both API and implementation stability are important to Envoy. Since the API is consumed by clients\\n44: beyond Envoy, it has a distinct set of [versioning guidelines](api/API_VERSIONING.md). Below, we\\n45: articulate the Envoy implementation stability rules, which operate within the context of the API\\n46: versioning guidelines:\\n47: \\n48: * Features may be marked as deprecated in a given versioned API at any point in time, but this may\\n49:   only be done when a replacement implementation and configuration path is available in Envoy on\\n50:   main. Deprecators must implement a conversion from the deprecated configuration to the latest\\n51:   `vNalpha` (with the deprecated field) that Envoy uses internally. A field may be deprecated if\\n52:   this tool would be able to perform the conversion. For example, removing a field to describe\\n53:   HTTP/2 window settings is valid if a more comprehensive HTTP/2 protocol options field is being\\n54:   introduced to replace it. The PR author deprecating the old configuration is responsible for\\n55:   updating all tests and canonical configuration, or guarding them with the\\n56:   `DEPRECATED_FEATURE_TEST()` macro. This will be validated by the `bazel.compile_time_options`\\n57:   target, which will hard-fail when deprecated configuration is used. The majority of tests and\\n58:   configuration for a feature should be expressed in terms of the latest Envoy internal\\n59:   configuration (i.e. `vNalpha`), only a minimal number of tests necessary to validate configuration\\n60:   translation should be guarded via the `DEPRECATED_FEATURE_TEST()` macro.\\n61: * We will delete deprecated configuration across major API versions. E.g. a field marked deprecated\\n62:   in v2 will be removed in v3.\\n63: * Unless the community and Envoy maintainer team agrees on an exception, during the\\n64:   first release cycle after a feature has been deprecated, use of that feature\\n65:   will cause a logged warning, and incrementing the\\n66:   [runtime](https://www.envoyproxy.io/docs/envoy/latest/configuration/operations/runtime#statistics)\\n67:   `runtime.deprecated_feature_use` stat.\\n68:   During the second release cycle, use of the deprecated configuration will\\n69:   cause a configuration load failure, unless the feature in question is\\n70:   explicitly overridden in\\n71:   [runtime](https://www.envoyproxy.io/docs/envoy/latest/configuration/operations/runtime#using-runtime-overrides-for-deprecated-features)\\n72:   config ([example](configs/using_deprecated_config.yaml)), or if\\n73:   `envoy.features.enable_all_deprecated_features` is set to true. Finally, following the deprecation\\n74:   of the API major version where the field was first marked deprecated, the entire implementation\\n75:   code will be removed from the Envoy implementation.\\n76: * If the runtime key `envoy.features.fail_on_any_deprecated_feature` is enabled,\\n77:   use of deprecated fields will trigger a configuration load failure\\n78:   rather than a logged warning.\\n79: * This policy means that organizations deploying main should have some time to get ready for\\n80:   breaking changes at the next major API version. This is typically a window of at least 12 months\\n81:   or until the organization moves to the next major API version.\\n82: * The breaking change policy also applies to source level extensions (e.g., filters). Code that\\n83:   conforms to the public interface documentation should continue to compile and work within the\\n84:   deprecation window. Within this window, a warning of deprecation should be carefully logged (some\\n85:   features might need rate limiting for logging this). We make no guarantees about code or deployments\\n86:   that rely on undocumented behavior. See [extension removal policy](./EXTENSION_POLICY.md#removing-existing-extensions)\\n87:   for more information.\\n88: * All deprecations/breaking changes will be clearly listed in the [version history](docs/root/version_history/).\\n89: * High risk deprecations/breaking changes may be announced to the\\n90:   [envoy-announce](https://groups.google.com/forum/#!forum/envoy-announce) email list but by default\\n91:   it is expected the multi-phase warn-by-default/fail-by-default is sufficient to warn users to move\\n92:   away from deprecated features.\\n93: \\n94: # Submitting a PR\\n95: \\n96: * Fork the repo.\\n97: * In your local repo, install the git hooks that implement various important pre-commit and\\n98:   pre-push checks:\\n99: \\n100:   ```\\n101:   ./support/bootstrap\\n102:   ```\\n103: \\n104:   Please see [support/README.md](support/README.md) for more information on these hooks.\\n105: \\n106: * Create your PR. If your PR adds new code, it should include tests [covering](source/docs/coverage.md) the new code. Please note that draft PRs may not be reviewed and will likely not be triaged, so do not create your PR as a draft if you want prompt reviews!\\n107: * Tests will automatically run for you.\\n108: * We will **not** merge any PR that is not passing tests.\\n109: * PRs are expected to have 100% test coverage for added code. This can be verified with a coverage\\n110:   build. If your PR cannot have 100% coverage for some reason please clearly explain why when you\\n111:   open it.\\n112: * Any PR that changes user-facing behavior **must** have associated documentation in [docs](docs) as\\n113:   well as [release notes](changelogs/current.yaml). API changes should be documented\\n114:   inline with protos as per the [API contribution guidelines](api/CONTRIBUTING.md). If a change applies\\n115:   to multiple sections of the release notes, it should be noted in the first (most important) section\\n116:   that applies. For instance, a bug fix that introduces incompatible behavior should be noted in\\n117:   `Incompatible Behavior Changes` but not in `Bug Fixes`.\\n118: * All code comments and documentation are expected to have proper English grammar and punctuation.\\n119:   If you are not a fluent English speaker (or a bad writer ;-)) please let us know and we will try\\n120:   to find some help but there are no guarantees.\\n121: * Your PR title should be descriptive, and generally start with a subsystem name followed by a\\n122:   colon. Examples:\\n123:   * \\\"docs: fix grammar error\\\"\\n124:   * \\\"http conn man: add new feature\\\"\\n125: * Your PR commit message will be used as the commit message when your PR is merged. You should\\n126:   update this field if your PR diverges during review.\\n127: * Your PR description should have details on what the PR does. If it fixes an existing issue it\\n128:   should end with \\\"Fixes #XXX\\\".\\n129: * If your PR is co-authored or based on an earlier PR from another contributor,\\n130:   please attribute them with `Co-authored-by: name <name@example.com>`. See\\n131:   GitHub's [multiple author\\n132:   guidance](https://help.github.com/en/github/committing-changes-to-your-project/creating-a-commit-with-multiple-authors)\\n133:   for further details.\\n134: * When all of the tests are passing and all other conditions described herein are satisfied, a\\n135:   maintainer will be assigned to review and merge the PR.\\n136: * Once your PR is under review, *please do not rebase it*. If you rebase, you will need to force push to\\n137:   github, and github's user interface will force your reviewer to review the PR\\n138:   from scratch rather than simply look at your latest changes.  It's much easier to review\\n139:   new commits and/or merges. We squash rebase the final merged commit so the number of commits\\n140:   you have in the PR don't matter. Again once your PR is assigned a reviewer, unless you need to fix DCO\\n141:   *please do not force push*.  If you need to pull recent changes you can run\\n142:   ```\\n143:   branch=$(git status|head -1|cut -f3 -d\\\\ )\\n144:   git checkout main\\n145:   git pull\\n146:   git checkout \\\"$branch\\\"\\n147:   git merge main\\n148:   ```\\n149: * We expect that once a PR is opened, it will be actively worked on until it is merged or closed.\\n150:   We reserve the right to close PRs that are not making progress. This is generally defined as no\\n151:   changes for 7 days. Obviously PRs that are closed due to lack of activity can be reopened later.\\n152:   Closing stale PRs helps us to keep on top of all of the work currently in flight.\\n153: * If a commit deprecates a feature, the commit message must mention what has been deprecated.\\n154:   Additionally, the [version history](changelogs/current.yaml) must be updated with\\n155:   relevant RST links for fields and messages as part of the commit.\\n156: * Please consider joining the [envoy-dev](https://groups.google.com/forum/#!forum/envoy-dev)\\n157:   mailing list.\\n158: * If your PR involves any changes to\\n159:   [envoy-filter-example](https://github.com/envoyproxy/envoy-filter-example) (for example making a new\\n160:   branch so that CI can pass) it is your responsibility to follow through with merging those\\n161:   changes back to main once the CI dance is done.\\n162: * If your PR is a high risk change, the reviewer may ask that you runtime guard\\n163:   it. See the section on runtime guarding below.\\n164: \\n165: \\n166: # Runtime guarding\\n167: \\n168: Some changes in Envoy are deemed worthy of runtime guarding. Instead of just replacing\\n169: old code with new code, both code paths are supported for between one Envoy release (if it is\\n170: guarded due to performance concerns) and a full deprecation cycle (if it is a high risk behavioral\\n171: change). Generally as a community we try to guard both high risk changes (major\\n172: refactors such as replacing Envoy's buffer implementation) and most user-visible\\n173: non-config-guarded changes to protocol processing (for example additions or changes to HTTP headers or\\n174: how HTTP is serialized out) for non-alpha features. Feel free to tag @envoyproxy/maintainers\\n175: if you aren't sure if a given change merits runtime guarding.\\n176: \\n177: The canonical way to runtime guard a feature is\\n178: ```\\n179: if (Runtime::runtimeFeatureEnabled(\\\"envoy.reloadable_features.my_feature_name\\\")) {\\n180:   [new code path]\\n181: } else {\\n182:   [old_code_path]\\n183: }\\n184: ```\\n185: Runtime guarded features named with the \\\"envoy.reloadable_features.\\\" prefix must be safe to flip\\n186: true or false on running Envoy instances. In some situations it may make more sense to\\n187: latch the value in a member variable on class creation, for example:\\n188: \\n189: ```\\n190: bool use_new_code_path_ =\\n191:     Runtime::runtimeFeatureEnabled(\\\"envoy.reloadable_features.my_feature_name\\\")\\n192: ```\\n193: \\n194: This should only be done if the lifetime of the object in question is relatively short compared to\\n195: the lifetime of most Envoy instances, i.e. latching state on creation of the\\n196: Http::ConnectionManagerImpl or all Network::ConnectionImpl classes, to ensure that the new behavior\\n197: will be exercised as the runtime value is flipped, and that the old behavior will trail off over\\n198: time.\\n199: \\n200: Runtime guarded features may either set true (running the new code by default) in the initial PR,\\n201: after a testing interval, or during the next release cycle, at the PR author's and reviewing\\n202: maintainer's discretion. Generally all runtime guarded features will be set true when a\\n203: release is cut. Old code paths for refactors can be cleaned up after a release and there has been\\n204: some production run time. Old code for behavioral changes will be deprecated after six months if no\\n205: Envoy operators have raised concerns. If the behavioral change is problematic for any Envoy users,\\n206: the maintainers team will work to find a satisfactory resolution, generally in the form of a permanent\\n207: configuration knob for the behavioral differences.\\n208: \\n209: Runtime features are set true by default by inclusion in\\n210: [source/common/runtime/runtime_features.cc](https://github.com/envoyproxy/envoy/blob/main/source/common/runtime/runtime_features.cc)\\n211: \\n212: There are four suggested options for testing new runtime features:\\n213: \\n214: 1. Create a per-test Runtime::LoaderSingleton as done in [DeprecatedFieldsTest.IndividualFieldDisallowedWithRuntimeOverride](https://github.com/envoyproxy/envoy/blob/main/test/common/protobuf/utility_test.cc)\\n215: 2. Create a [parameterized test](https://github.com/google/googletest/blob/master/docs/advanced.md#how-to-write-value-parameterized-tests)\\n216:    where the set up of the test sets the new runtime value explicitly to\\n217:    GetParam() as outlined in (1).\\n218: 3. Set up integration tests with custom runtime defaults as documented in the\\n219:    [integration test README](https://github.com/envoyproxy/envoy/blob/main/test/integration/README.md)\\n220: 4. Run a given unit test with the new runtime value explicitly set true or false as done\\n221:    for [runtime_flag_override_test](https://github.com/envoyproxy/envoy/blob/main/test/common/runtime/BUILD)\\n222: \\n223: Runtime code is held to the same standard as regular Envoy code, so both the old\\n224: path and the new should have 100% coverage both with the feature defaulting true\\n225: and false.\\n226: \\n227: Please note that if adding a runtime guarded feature, your [release notes](changelogs/current.yaml) should include both the functional change, and how to revert it, for example\\n228: \\n229: ```yaml\\n230: - area: config\\n231:   change: |\\n232:       type URL is used to lookup extensions regardless of the name field. This may cause problems for empty filter configurations or mis-matched protobuf as the typed configurations. This behavioral change can be temporarily reverted by setting runtime guard ``envoy.reloadable_features.no_extension_lookup_by_name`` to false.\\n233: ```\\n234: \\n235: # PR review policy for maintainers\\n236: \\n237: * Typically we try to turn around reviews within one business day.\\n238: * See [OWNERS.md](OWNERS.md) for the current list of maintainers.\\n239: * It is generally expected that a senior maintainer should review every PR to\\n240:   core code. Changes which only touch tests, extensions, tools, docs or comments\\n241:   need only be reviewed by a maintainer, or senior extension maintainer.\\n242: * It is also generally expected that a \\\"domain expert\\\" for the code the PR touches should review the\\n243:   PR. This person does not necessarily need to have commit access.\\n244: * For new extensions (contrib or otherwise) and features, at least one of the approvals should be *from an\\n245:   organization different from the PR author.* E.g., if Lyft authors a PR, at least one approver\\n246:   should be from an organization other than Lyft. This helps us make sure that we aren't putting\\n247:   organization specific shortcuts into the code.\\n248:   new HTTP/3 features are largely exempt from cross-company approvals as all of the\\n249:   area experts work at a single company, but HTTP/3 changes which impact general\\n250:   functionality still merit a cross-company check.\\n251: * contrib extensions do not need senior maintainer or maintainer review only contrib owner review and\\n252:   a maintainer stamp to merge.\\n253: * If there is a question on who should review a PR please discuss in Slack.\\n254: * Anyone is welcome to review any PR that they want, whether they are a maintainer or not.\\n255: * Please make sure that the PR title, commit message, and description are updated if the PR changes\\n256:   significantly during review.\\n257: * Please **clean up the title and body** before merging. By default, GitHub fills the squash merge\\n258:   title with the original title, and the commit body with every individual commit from the PR.\\n259:   The maintainer doing the merge should make sure the title follows the guidelines above and should\\n260:   overwrite the body with the original commit message from the PR (cleaning it up if necessary)\\n261:   while preserving the PR author's final DCO sign-off.\\n262: * If a PR includes a deprecation/breaking change, notification should be sent to the\\n263:   [envoy-announce](https://groups.google.com/forum/#!forum/envoy-announce) email list.\\n264: \\n265: # API changes\\n266: \\n267: If you change anything in the [api tree](https://github.com/envoyproxy/envoy/tree/main/api),\\n268: please read the [API Review\\n269: Checklist](https://github.com/envoyproxy/envoy/tree/main/api/review_checklist.md)\\n270: and make sure that your changes have addressed all of the considerations listed there.\\n271: \\n272: # Adding new extensions\\n273: \\n274: For developers adding a new extension, one can take an existing extension as the starting point.\\n275: \\n276: Extension configuration should be located in a directory structure like\\n277: `api/envoy/extensions/area/plugin/`, for example `api/envoy/extensions/access_loggers/file/`\\n278: \\n279: The code for the extension should be located under the equivalent\\n280: `source/extensions/area/plugin`, and include an *envoy_cc_extension* with the\\n281: configuration and tagged with the appropriate security posture, and an\\n282: *envoy_cc_library* with the code.\\n283: \\n284: More details on how to add a new extension API can be found [here](api/STYLE.md#adding-an-extension-configuration-to-the-api):\\n285: \\n286: # Adding contrib extensions\\n287: \\n288: See [EXTENSION_POLICY.md](EXTENSION_POLICY.md) for more information on contrib. Adding a contrib\\n289: extension mostly mirrors adding a normal extension above. Some differences are noted here:\\n290: \\n291: * API files should be added in `api/contrib/envoy/`, but the protos' namespaces should still be as\\n292:   in normal extensions (which will make file movement easier later if the extension gets promoted\\n293:   to core).\\n294: * Build config and metadata should be included in [contrib/contrib_build_config.bzl](contrib/contrib_build_config.bzl)\\n295:   and [contrib/extensions_metadata.yaml](contrib/extensions_metadata.yaml).\\n296: * An entrypoint should be added in `docs/root/api-v3/config/contrib/contrib.rst`\\n297: \\n298: # DCO: Sign your work\\n299: \\n300: Envoy ships commit hooks that allow you to auto-generate the DCO signoff line if\\n301: it doesn't exist when you run `git commit`. Simply navigate to the Envoy project\\n302: root and run:\\n303: \\n304: ```bash\\n305: ./support/bootstrap\\n306: ```\\n307: \\n308: From here, simply commit as normal, and you will see the signoff at the bottom\\n309: of each commit.\\n310: \\n311: The sign-off is a simple line at the end of the explanation for the\\n312: patch, which certifies that you wrote it or otherwise have the right to\\n313: pass it on as an open-source patch. The rules are pretty simple: if you\\n314: can certify the below (from\\n315: [developercertificate.org](https://developercertificate.org/)):\\n316: \\n317: ```\\n318: Developer Certificate of Origin\\n319: Version 1.1\\n320: \\n321: Copyright (C) 2004, 2006 The Linux Foundation and its contributors.\\n322: 660 York Street, Suite 102,\\n323: San Francisco, CA 94110 USA\\n324: \\n325: Everyone is permitted to copy and distribute verbatim copies of this\\n326: license document, but changing it is not allowed.\\n327: \\n328: \\n329: Developer's Certificate of Origin 1.1\\n330: \\n331: By making a contribution to this project, I certify that:\\n332: \\n333: (a) The contribution was created in whole or in part by me and I\\n334:     have the right to submit it under the open source license\\n335:     indicated in the file; or\\n336: \\n337: (b) The contribution is based upon previous work that, to the best\\n338:     of my knowledge, is covered under an appropriate open source\\n339:     license and I have the right under that license to submit that\\n340:     work with modifications, whether created in whole or in part\\n341:     by me, under the same open source license (unless I am\\n342:     permitted to submit under a different license), as indicated\\n343:     in the file; or\\n344: \\n345: (c) The contribution was provided directly to me by some other\\n346:     person who certified (a), (b) or (c) and I have not modified\\n347:     it.\\n348: \\n349: (d) I understand and agree that this project and the contribution\\n350:     are public and that a record of the contribution (including all\\n351:     personal information I submit with it, including my sign-off) is\\n352:     maintained indefinitely and may be redistributed consistent with\\n353:     this project or the open source license(s) involved.\\n354: ```\\n355: \\n356: then you just add a line to every git commit message:\\n357: \\n358:     Signed-off-by: Joe Smith <joe@gmail.com>\\n359: \\n360: using your real name (sorry, no pseudonyms or anonymous contributions.)\\n361: \\n362: You can add the sign off when creating the git commit via `git commit -s`.\\n363: \\n364: If you want this to be automatic you can set up some aliases:\\n365: \\n366: ```bash\\n367: git config --add alias.amend \\\"commit -s --amend\\\"\\n368: git config --add alias.c \\\"commit -s\\\"\\n369: ```\\n370: \\n371: ## Fixing DCO\\n372: \\n373: If your PR fails the DCO check, it's necessary to fix the entire commit history in the PR. Best\\n374: practice is to [squash](https://gitready.com/advanced/2009/02/10/squashing-commits-with-rebase.html)\\n375: the commit history to a single commit, append the DCO sign-off as described above, and [force\\n376: push](https://git-scm.com/docs/git-push#git-push---force). For example, if you have 2 commits in\\n377: your history:\\n378: \\n379: ```bash\\n380: git rebase -i HEAD^^\\n381: (interactive squash + DCO append)\\n382: git push origin -f\\n383: ```\\n384: \\n385: Note, that in general rewriting history in this way is a hindrance to the review process and this\\n386: should only be done to correct a DCO mistake.\\n387: \\n388: ## Triggering CI re-run without making changes\\n389: \\n390: To rerun failed tasks in Azure pipelines, add a comment with the line\\n391: \\n392: ```\\n393: /retest\\n394: ```\\n395: \\n396: in it. This should rebuild only the failed tasks.\\n397: \\n398: Sometimes tasks will be stuck in CI and won't be marked as failed, which means\\n399: the above command won't work. Should this happen, pushing an empty commit should\\n400: re-run all the CI tasks. Consider adding an alias into your `.gitconfig` file:\\n401: \\n402: ```\\n403: [alias]\\n404:     kick-ci = !\\\"git commit -s --allow-empty -m 'Kick CI' && git push\\\"\\n405: ```\\n406: \\n407: Once you add this alias you can issue the command `git kick-ci` and the PR\\n408: will be sent back for a retest.\\n409: \\n410: # Repo Etiquette\\n411: \\n412: Contributors with push-access to the Envoy project should prefer pushing changes to a personal fork,\\n413: including when creating branches for pull requests.\\n414: \\n415: This helps keep the Envoy repo as lean as possible, which can speed up cloning and synchronizing\\n416: operations for both developers and CI.\\n417: \",\"url\":\"https://sourcegraph.sourcegraph.com/github.com/sg-evals/envoy--v1.32.1@b35dd17bea856e19fc4e65fb05e68170841d3726/-/blob/CONTRIBUTING.md\"}","structuredContent":{"content":"1: We welcome contributions from the community. Please read the following guidelines carefully to\n2: maximize the chances of your PR being merged.\n3: \n4: # Communication\n5: \n6: * Before starting work on a major feature, please reach out to us via GitHub, Slack,\n7:   email, etc. We will make sure no one else is already working on it and ask you to open a\n8:   GitHub issue.\n9: * A \"major feature\" is defined as any change that is > 100 LOC altered (not including tests), or\n10:   changes any user-facing behavior. We will use the GitHub issue to discuss the feature and come to\n11:   agreement. This is to prevent your time being wasted, as well as ours. The GitHub review process\n12:   for major features is also important so that [organizations with commit access](OWNERS.md) can\n13:   come to agreement on design. If it is appropriate to write a design document, the document must\n14:   be hosted either in the GitHub tracking issue, or linked to from the issue and hosted in a\n15:   world-readable location.\n16: * Specifically, if the goal is to add a new [extension](REPO_LAYOUT.md#sourceextensions-layout),\n17:   please read the [extension policy](GOVERNANCE.md#extension-addition-policy).\n18: * Small patches and bug fixes don't need prior communication.\n19: \n20: # Coding style\n21: \n22: * See [STYLE.md](STYLE.md)\n23: \n24: # Inclusive language policy\n25: \n26: The Envoy community has an explicit goal to be inclusive to all. As such, all PRs must adhere to the\n27: following guidelines for all code, APIs, and documentation:\n28: \n29: * The following words and phrases are not allowed:\n30:   * *Whitelist*: use allowlist instead.\n31:   * *Blacklist*: use denylist or blocklist instead.\n32:   * *Master*: use primary or main instead.\n33:   * *Slave*: use secondary or replica instead.\n34: * Documentation should be written in an inclusive style. The [Google developer\n35:   documentation](https://developers.google.com/style/inclusive-documentation) contains an excellent\n36:   reference on this topic.\n37: * The above policy is not considered definitive and may be amended in the future as industry best\n38:   practices evolve. Additional comments on this topic may be provided by maintainers during code\n39:   review.\n40: \n41: # Breaking change policy\n42: \n43: Both API and implementation stability are important to Envoy. Since the API is consumed by clients\n44: beyond Envoy, it has a distinct set of [versioning guidelines](api/API_VERSIONING.md). Below, we\n45: articulate the Envoy implementation stability rules, which operate within the context of the API\n46: versioning guidelines:\n47: \n48: * Features may be marked as deprecated in a given versioned API at any point in time, but this may\n49:   only be done when a replacement implementation and configuration path is available in Envoy on\n50:   main. Deprecators must implement a conversion from the deprecated configuration to the latest\n51:   `vNalpha` (with the deprecated field) that Envoy uses internally. A field may be deprecated if\n52:   this tool would be able to perform the conversion. For example, removing a field to describe\n53:   HTTP/2 window settings is valid if a more comprehensive HTTP/2 protocol options field is being\n54:   introduced to replace it. The PR author deprecating the old configuration is responsible for\n55:   updating all tests and canonical configuration, or guarding them with the\n56:   `DEPRECATED_FEATURE_TEST()` macro. This will be validated by the `bazel.compile_time_options`\n57:   target, which will hard-fail when deprecated configuration is used. The majority of tests and\n58:   configuration for a feature should be expressed in terms of the latest Envoy internal\n59:   configuration (i.e. `vNalpha`), only a minimal number of tests necessary to validate configuration\n60:   translation should be guarded via the `DEPRECATED_FEATURE_TEST()` macro.\n61: * We will delete deprecated configuration across major API versions. E.g. a field marked deprecated\n62:   in v2 will be removed in v3.\n63: * Unless the community and Envoy maintainer team agrees on an exception, during the\n64:   first release cycle after a feature has been deprecated, use of that feature\n65:   will cause a logged warning, and incrementing the\n66:   [runtime](https://www.envoyproxy.io/docs/envoy/latest/configuration/operations/runtime#statistics)\n67:   `runtime.deprecated_feature_use` stat.\n68:   During the second release cycle, use of the deprecated configuration will\n69:   cause a configuration load failure, unless the feature in question is\n70:   explicitly overridden in\n71:   [runtime](https://www.envoyproxy.io/docs/envoy/latest/configuration/operations/runtime#using-runtime-overrides-for-deprecated-features)\n72:   config ([example](configs/using_deprecated_config.yaml)), or if\n73:   `envoy.features.enable_all_deprecated_features` is set to true. Finally, following the deprecation\n74:   of the API major version where the field was first marked deprecated, the entire implementation\n75:   code will be removed from the Envoy implementation.\n76: * If the runtime key `envoy.features.fail_on_any_deprecated_feature` is enabled,\n77:   use of deprecated fields will trigger a configuration load failure\n78:   rather than a logged warning.\n79: * This policy means that organizations deploying main should have some time to get ready for\n80:   breaking changes at the next major API version. This is typically a window of at least 12 months\n81:   or until the organization moves to the next major API version.\n82: * The breaking change policy also applies to source level extensions (e.g., filters). Code that\n83:   conforms to the public interface documentation should continue to compile and work within the\n84:   deprecation window. Within this window, a warning of deprecation should be carefully logged (some\n85:   features might need rate limiting for logging this). We make no guarantees about code or deployments\n86:   that rely on undocumented behavior. See [extension removal policy](./EXTENSION_POLICY.md#removing-existing-extensions)\n87:   for more information.\n88: * All deprecations/breaking changes will be clearly listed in the [version history](docs/root/version_history/).\n89: * High risk deprecations/breaking changes may be announced to the\n90:   [envoy-announce](https://groups.google.com/forum/#!forum/envoy-announce) email list but by default\n91:   it is expected the multi-phase warn-by-default/fail-by-default is sufficient to warn users to move\n92:   away from deprecated features.\n93: \n94: # Submitting a PR\n95: \n96: * Fork the repo.\n97: * In your local repo, install the git hooks that implement various important pre-commit and\n98:   pre-push checks:\n99: \n100:   ```\n101:   ./support/bootstrap\n102:   ```\n103: \n104:   Please see [support/README.md](support/README.md) for more information on these hooks.\n105: \n106: * Create your PR. If your PR adds new code, it should include tests [covering](source/docs/coverage.md) the new code. Please note that draft PRs may not be reviewed and will likely not be triaged, so do not create your PR as a draft if you want prompt reviews!\n107: * Tests will automatically run for you.\n108: * We will **not** merge any PR that is not passing tests.\n109: * PRs are expected to have 100% test coverage for added code. This can be verified with a coverage\n110:   build. If your PR cannot have 100% coverage for some reason please clearly explain why when you\n111:   open it.\n112: * Any PR that changes user-facing behavior **must** have associated documentation in [docs](docs) as\n113:   well as [release notes](changelogs/current.yaml). API changes should be documented\n114:   inline with protos as per the [API contribution guidelines](api/CONTRIBUTING.md). If a change applies\n115:   to multiple sections of the release notes, it should be noted in the first (most important) section\n116:   that applies. For instance, a bug fix that introduces incompatible behavior should be noted in\n117:   `Incompatible Behavior Changes` but not in `Bug Fixes`.\n118: * All code comments and documentation are expected to have proper English grammar and punctuation.\n119:   If you are not a fluent English speaker (or a bad writer ;-)) please let us know and we will try\n120:   to find some help but there are no guarantees.\n121: * Your PR title should be descriptive, and generally start with a subsystem name followed by a\n122:   colon. Examples:\n123:   * \"docs: fix grammar error\"\n124:   * \"http conn man: add new feature\"\n125: * Your PR commit message will be used as the commit message when your PR is merged. You should\n126:   update this field if your PR diverges during review.\n127: * Your PR description should have details on what the PR does. If it fixes an existing issue it\n128:   should end with \"Fixes #XXX\".\n129: * If your PR is co-authored or based on an earlier PR from another contributor,\n130:   please attribute them with `Co-authored-by: name <name@example.com>`. See\n131:   GitHub's [multiple author\n132:   guidance](https://help.github.com/en/github/committing-changes-to-your-project/creating-a-commit-with-multiple-authors)\n133:   for further details.\n134: * When all of the tests are passing and all other conditions described herein are satisfied, a\n135:   maintainer will be assigned to review and merge the PR.\n136: * Once your PR is under review, *please do not rebase it*. If you rebase, you will need to force push to\n137:   github, and github's user interface will force your reviewer to review the PR\n138:   from scratch rather than simply look at your latest changes.  It's much easier to review\n139:   new commits and/or merges. We squash rebase the final merged commit so the number of commits\n140:   you have in the PR don't matter. Again once your PR is assigned a reviewer, unless you need to fix DCO\n141:   *please do not force push*.  If you need to pull recent changes you can run\n142:   ```\n143:   branch=$(git status|head -1|cut -f3 -d\\ )\n144:   git checkout main\n145:   git pull\n146:   git checkout \"$branch\"\n147:   git merge main\n148:   ```\n149: * We expect that once a PR is opened, it will be actively worked on until it is merged or closed.\n150:   We reserve the right to close PRs that are not making progress. This is generally defined as no\n151:   changes for 7 days. Obviously PRs that are closed due to lack of activity can be reopened later.\n152:   Closing stale PRs helps us to keep on top of all of the work currently in flight.\n153: * If a commit deprecates a feature, the commit message must mention what has been deprecated.\n154:   Additionally, the [version history](changelogs/current.yaml) must be updated with\n155:   relevant RST links for fields and messages as part of the commit.\n156: * Please consider joining the [envoy-dev](https://groups.google.com/forum/#!forum/envoy-dev)\n157:   mailing list.\n158: * If your PR involves any changes to\n159:   [envoy-filter-example](https://github.com/envoyproxy/envoy-filter-example) (for example making a new\n160:   branch so that CI can pass) it is your responsibility to follow through with merging those\n161:   changes back to main once the CI dance is done.\n162: * If your PR is a high risk change, the reviewer may ask that you runtime guard\n163:   it. See the section on runtime guarding below.\n164: \n165: \n166: # Runtime guarding\n167: \n168: Some changes in Envoy are deemed worthy of runtime guarding. Instead of just replacing\n169: old code with new code, both code paths are supported for between one Envoy release (if it is\n170: guarded due to performance concerns) and a full deprecation cycle (if it is a high risk behavioral\n171: change). Generally as a community we try to guard both high risk changes (major\n172: refactors such as replacing Envoy's buffer implementation) and most user-visible\n173: non-config-guarded changes to protocol processing (for example additions or changes to HTTP headers or\n174: how HTTP is serialized out) for non-alpha features. Feel free to tag @envoyproxy/maintainers\n175: if you aren't sure if a given change merits runtime guarding.\n176: \n177: The canonical way to runtime guard a feature is\n178: ```\n179: if (Runtime::runtimeFeatureEnabled(\"envoy.reloadable_features.my_feature_name\")) {\n180:   [new code path]\n181: } else {\n182:   [old_code_path]\n183: }\n184: ```\n185: Runtime guarded features named with the \"envoy.reloadable_features.\" prefix must be safe to flip\n186: true or false on running Envoy instances. In some situations it may make more sense to\n187: latch the value in a member variable on class creation, for example:\n188: \n189: ```\n190: bool use_new_code_path_ =\n191:     Runtime::runtimeFeatureEnabled(\"envoy.reloadable_features.my_feature_name\")\n192: ```\n193: \n194: This should only be done if the lifetime of the object in question is relatively short compared to\n195: the lifetime of most Envoy instances, i.e. latching state on creation of the\n196: Http::ConnectionManagerImpl or all Network::ConnectionImpl classes, to ensure that the new behavior\n197: will be exercised as the runtime value is flipped, and that the old behavior will trail off over\n198: time.\n199: \n200: Runtime guarded features may either set true (running the new code by default) in the initial PR,\n201: after a testing interval, or during the next release cycle, at the PR author's and reviewing\n202: maintainer's discretion. Generally all runtime guarded features will be set true when a\n203: release is cut. Old code paths for refactors can be cleaned up after a release and there has been\n204: some production run time. Old code for behavioral changes will be deprecated after six months if no\n205: Envoy operators have raised concerns. If the behavioral change is problematic for any Envoy users,\n206: the maintainers team will work to find a satisfactory resolution, generally in the form of a permanent\n207: configuration knob for the behavioral differences.\n208: \n209: Runtime features are set true by default by inclusion in\n210: [source/common/runtime/runtime_features.cc](https://github.com/envoyproxy/envoy/blob/main/source/common/runtime/runtime_features.cc)\n211: \n212: There are four suggested options for testing new runtime features:\n213: \n214: 1. Create a per-test Runtime::LoaderSingleton as done in [DeprecatedFieldsTest.IndividualFieldDisallowedWithRuntimeOverride](https://github.com/envoyproxy/envoy/blob/main/test/common/protobuf/utility_test.cc)\n215: 2. Create a [parameterized test](https://github.com/google/googletest/blob/master/docs/advanced.md#how-to-write-value-parameterized-tests)\n216:    where the set up of the test sets the new runtime value explicitly to\n217:    GetParam() as outlined in (1).\n218: 3. Set up integration tests with custom runtime defaults as documented in the\n219:    [integration test README](https://github.com/envoyproxy/envoy/blob/main/test/integration/README.md)\n220: 4. Run a given unit test with the new runtime value explicitly set true or false as done\n221:    for [runtime_flag_override_test](https://github.com/envoyproxy/envoy/blob/main/test/common/runtime/BUILD)\n222: \n223: Runtime code is held to the same standard as regular Envoy code, so both the old\n224: path and the new should have 100% coverage both with the feature defaulting true\n225: and false.\n226: \n227: Please note that if adding a runtime guarded feature, your [release notes](changelogs/current.yaml) should include both the functional change, and how to revert it, for example\n228: \n229: ```yaml\n230: - area: config\n231:   change: |\n232:       type URL is used to lookup extensions regardless of the name field. This may cause problems for empty filter configurations or mis-matched protobuf as the typed configurations. This behavioral change can be temporarily reverted by setting runtime guard ``envoy.reloadable_features.no_extension_lookup_by_name`` to false.\n233: ```\n234: \n235: # PR review policy for maintainers\n236: \n237: * Typically we try to turn around reviews within one business day.\n238: * See [OWNERS.md](OWNERS.md) for the current list of maintainers.\n239: * It is generally expected that a senior maintainer should review every PR to\n240:   core code. Changes which only touch tests, extensions, tools, docs or comments\n241:   need only be reviewed by a maintainer, or senior extension maintainer.\n242: * It is also generally expected that a \"domain expert\" for the code the PR touches should review the\n243:   PR. This person does not necessarily need to have commit access.\n244: * For new extensions (contrib or otherwise) and features, at least one of the approvals should be *from an\n245:   organization different from the PR author.* E.g., if Lyft authors a PR, at least one approver\n246:   should be from an organization other than Lyft. This helps us make sure that we aren't putting\n247:   organization specific shortcuts into the code.\n248:   new HTTP/3 features are largely exempt from cross-company approvals as all of the\n249:   area experts work at a single company, but HTTP/3 changes which impact general\n250:   functionality still merit a cross-company check.\n251: * contrib extensions do not need senior maintainer or maintainer review only contrib owner review and\n252:   a maintainer stamp to merge.\n253: * If there is a question on who should review a PR please discuss in Slack.\n254: * Anyone is welcome to review any PR that they want, whether they are a maintainer or not.\n255: * Please make sure that the PR title, commit message, and description are updated if the PR changes\n256:   significantly during review.\n257: * Please **clean up the title and body** before merging. By default, GitHub fills the squash merge\n258:   title with the original title, and the commit body with every individual commit from the PR.\n259:   The maintainer doing the merge should make sure the title follows the guidelines above and should\n260:   overwrite the body with the original commit message from the PR (cleaning it up if necessary)\n261:   while preserving the PR author's final DCO sign-off.\n262: * If a PR includes a deprecation/breaking change, notification should be sent to the\n263:   [envoy-announce](https://groups.google.com/forum/#!forum/envoy-announce) email list.\n264: \n265: # API changes\n266: \n267: If you change anything in the [api tree](https://github.com/envoyproxy/envoy/tree/main/api),\n268: please read the [API Review\n269: Checklist](https://github.com/envoyproxy/envoy/tree/main/api/review_checklist.md)\n270: and make sure that your changes have addressed all of the considerations listed there.\n271: \n272: # Adding new extensions\n273: \n274: For developers adding a new extension, one can take an existing extension as the starting point.\n275: \n276: Extension configuration should be located in a directory structure like\n277: `api/envoy/extensions/area/plugin/`, for example `api/envoy/extensions/access_loggers/file/`\n278: \n279: The code for the extension should be located under the equivalent\n280: `source/extensions/area/plugin`, and include an *envoy_cc_extension* with the\n281: configuration and tagged with the appropriate security posture, and an\n282: *envoy_cc_library* with the code.\n283: \n284: More details on how to add a new extension API can be found [here](api/STYLE.md#adding-an-extension-configuration-to-the-api):\n285: \n286: # Adding contrib extensions\n287: \n288: See [EXTENSION_POLICY.md](EXTENSION_POLICY.md) for more information on contrib. Adding a contrib\n289: extension mostly mirrors adding a normal extension above. Some differences are noted here:\n290: \n291: * API files should be added in `api/contrib/envoy/`, but the protos' namespaces should still be as\n292:   in normal extensions (which will make file movement easier later if the extension gets promoted\n293:   to core).\n294: * Build config and metadata should be included in [contrib/contrib_build_config.bzl](contrib/contrib_build_config.bzl)\n295:   and [contrib/extensions_metadata.yaml](contrib/extensions_metadata.yaml).\n296: * An entrypoint should be added in `docs/root/api-v3/config/contrib/contrib.rst`\n297: \n298: # DCO: Sign your work\n299: \n300: Envoy ships commit hooks that allow you to auto-generate the DCO signoff line if\n301: it doesn't exist when you run `git commit`. Simply navigate to the Envoy project\n302: root and run:\n303: \n304: ```bash\n305: ./support/bootstrap\n306: ```\n307: \n308: From here, simply commit as normal, and you will see the signoff at the bottom\n309: of each commit.\n310: \n311: The sign-off is a simple line at the end of the explanation for the\n312: patch, which certifies that you wrote it or otherwise have the right to\n313: pass it on as an open-source patch. The rules are pretty simple: if you\n314: can certify the below (from\n315: [developercertificate.org](https://developercertificate.org/)):\n316: \n317: ```\n318: Developer Certificate of Origin\n319: Version 1.1\n320: \n321: Copyright (C) 2004, 2006 The Linux Foundation and its contributors.\n322: 660 York Street, Suite 102,\n323: San Francisco, CA 94110 USA\n324: \n325: Everyone is permitted to copy and distribute verbatim copies of this\n326: license document, but changing it is not allowed.\n327: \n328: \n329: Developer's Certificate of Origin 1.1\n330: \n331: By making a contribution to this project, I certify that:\n332: \n333: (a) The contribution was created in whole or in part by me and I\n334:     have the right to submit it under the open source license\n335:     indicated in the file; or\n336: \n337: (b) The contribution is based upon previous work that, to the best\n338:     of my knowledge, is covered under an appropriate open source\n339:     license and I have the right under that license to submit that\n340:     work with modifications, whether created in whole or in part\n341:     by me, under the same open source license (unless I am\n342:     permitted to submit under a different license), as indicated\n343:     in the file; or\n344: \n345: (c) The contribution was provided directly to me by some other\n346:     person who certified (a), (b) or (c) and I have not modified\n347:     it.\n348: \n349: (d) I understand and agree that this project and the contribution\n350:     are public and that a record of the contribution (including all\n351:     personal information I submit with it, including my sign-off) is\n352:     maintained indefinitely and may be redistributed consistent with\n353:     this project or the open source license(s) involved.\n354: ```\n355: \n356: then you just add a line to every git commit message:\n357: \n358:     Signed-off-by: Joe Smith <joe@gmail.com>\n359: \n360: using your real name (sorry, no pseudonyms or anonymous contributions.)\n361: \n362: You can add the sign off when creating the git commit via `git commit -s`.\n363: \n364: If you want this to be automatic you can set up some aliases:\n365: \n366: ```bash\n367: git config --add alias.amend \"commit -s --amend\"\n368: git config --add alias.c \"commit -s\"\n369: ```\n370: \n371: ## Fixing DCO\n372: \n373: If your PR fails the DCO check, it's necessary to fix the entire commit history in the PR. Best\n374: practice is to [squash](https://gitready.com/advanced/2009/02/10/squashing-commits-with-rebase.html)\n375: the commit history to a single commit, append the DCO sign-off as described above, and [force\n376: push](https://git-scm.com/docs/git-push#git-push---force). For example, if you have 2 commits in\n377: your history:\n378: \n379: ```bash\n380: git rebase -i HEAD^^\n381: (interactive squash + DCO append)\n382: git push origin -f\n383: ```\n384: \n385: Note, that in general rewriting history in this way is a hindrance to the review process and this\n386: should only be done to correct a DCO mistake.\n387: \n388: ## Triggering CI re-run without making changes\n389: \n390: To rerun failed tasks in Azure pipelines, add a comment with the line\n391: \n392: ```\n393: /retest\n394: ```\n395: \n396: in it. This should rebuild only the failed tasks.\n397: \n398: Sometimes tasks will be stuck in CI and won't be marked as failed, which means\n399: the above command won't work. Should this happen, pushing an empty commit should\n400: re-run all the CI tasks. Consider adding an alias into your `.gitconfig` file:\n401: \n402: ```\n403: [alias]\n404:     kick-ci = !\"git commit -s --allow-empty -m 'Kick CI' && git push\"\n405: ```\n406: \n407: Once you add this alias you can issue the command `git kick-ci` and the PR\n408: will be sent back for a retest.\n409: \n410: # Repo Etiquette\n411: \n412: Contributors with push-access to the Envoy project should prefer pushing changes to a personal fork,\n413: including when creating branches for pull requests.\n414: \n415: This helps keep the Envoy repo as lean as possible, which can speed up cloning and synchronizing\n416: operations for both developers and CI.\n417: ","url":"https://sourcegraph.sourcegraph.com/github.com/sg-evals/envoy--v1.32.1@b35dd17bea856e19fc4e65fb05e68170841d3726/-/blob/CONTRIBUTING.md"}}}

Configure, build and/or install the [Envoy dependencies](https://www.envoyproxy.io/docs/envoy/latest/start/building#requirements).\\n33: 1. `bazel build -c opt envoy` from the repository root.\\n34: \\n35: ### Building from a release tarball\\n36: \\n37: To build Envoy from a release tarball, you can download a release tarball from Assets section in each release in project [Releases page](https://github.com/envoyproxy/envoy/releases).\\n38: Given all required [Envoy dependencies](https://www.envoyproxy.io/docs/envoy/latest/start/building#requirements) are installed, the following steps should be followed:\\n39: \\n40: 1. Download and extract source code of a release tarball from the Releases page. For example: https://github.com/envoyproxy/envoy/releases/tag/v1.24.0.\\n41: 1. `python3 tools/github/write_current_source_version.py` from the repository root.\\n42: 1. `bazel build -c opt envoy` from the repository root.\\n43: \\n44: > **Note**: If the the `write_current_source_version.py` script is missing from the extracted source code directory, you can download it from [here](https://raw.githubusercontent.com/envoyproxy/envoy/main/tools/github/write_current_source_version.py).\\n45: > This script is used to generate SOURCE_VERSION that is required by [`bazel/get_workspace_status`](./get_workspace_status) to \\\"stamp\\\" the binary in a non-git directory.\\n46: \\n47: > **Note**: To avoid rate-limiting by GitHub API, you can provide [a valid GitHub token](https://docs.github.com/en/authentication/keeping-your-account-and-data-secure/about-authentication-to-github#githubs-token-formats) to `GITHUB_TOKEN` environment variable.\\n48: > The environment variable name that holds the token can also be customized by setting `--github_api_token_env_name`.\\n49: > In a GitHub Actions workflow file, you can set this token from [`secrets.GITHUB_TOKEN`](https://docs.github.com/en/actions/security-guides/automatic-token-authentication#about-the-github_token-secret).\\n50: \\n51: Examples:\\n52: \\n53: ```console\\n54: GITHUB_TOKEN=<GITHUB_TOKEN> python3 tools/github/write_current_source_version.py\\n55: MY_TOKEN=<GITHUB_TOKEN> python3 tools/github/write_current_source_version.py --github_api_token_env_name=MY_TOKEN\\n56: ```\\n57: \\n58: ## Quick start Bazel build for developers\\n59: \\n60: This section describes how to and what dependencies to install to get started building Envoy with Bazel.\\n61: If you would rather use a pre-build Docker image with required tools installed, skip to [this section](#building-envoy-with-the-ci-docker-image).\\n62: \\n63: As a developer convenience, a [WORKSPACE](https://github.com/envoyproxy/envoy/blob/main/WORKSPACE) and\\n64: [rules for building a recent\\n65: version](https://github.com/envoyproxy/envoy/blob/main/bazel/repositories.bzl) of the various Envoy\\n66: dependencies are provided. These are provided as is, they are only suitable for development and\\n67: testing purposes.
