If the\n597: stack trace is not symbolized, try setting the ASAN_SYMBOLIZER_PATH environment variable to point to the\n598: llvm-symbolizer binary (or make sure the llvm-symbolizer is in your $PATH).\n599: \n600: If you have clang-5.0 or newer, additional checks are provided with:\n601: \n602: ```\n603: bazel test -c dbg --config=clang-asan //test/...\n604: ```\n605: \n606: [Thread sanitizer (TSAN)](https://github.com/google/sanitizers/wiki/ThreadSanitizerCppManual) tests rely on\n607: a TSAN-instrumented version of libc++ and can be run under the docker sandbox:\n608: \n609: ```\n610: bazel test -c dbg --config=docker-tsan //test/...\n611: ```\n612: \n613: Alternatively, you can build a local copy of TSAN-instrumented libc++. Follow the [quick start](#quick-start-bazel-build-for-developers) instruction to setup Clang+LLVM environment. Download LLVM sources from the [LLVM official site](https://github.com/llvm/llvm-project)\n614: \n615: ```\n616: curl -sSfL \"https://github.com/llvm/llvm-project/archive/llvmorg-11.0.1.tar.gz\" | tar zx\n617: \n618: ```\n619: \n620: Configure and build a TSAN-instrumented libc++. Please note that `LLVM_USE_SANITIZER=Thread` preprocessor definition is used to enable TSAN instrumentation, and `CMAKE_INSTALL_PREFIX=\"/opt/libcxx_tsan\"` defines the installation directory path.\n621: \n622: ```\n623: mkdir tsan\n624: pushd tsan\n625: \n626: cmake -GNinja -DLLVM_ENABLE_PROJECTS=\"libcxxabi;libcxx\" -DLLVM_USE_LINKER=lld -DLLVM_USE_SANITIZER=Thread -DCMAKE_BUILD_TYPE=Release \\\n627:   -DCMAKE_C_COMPILER=clang -DCMAKE_CXX_COMPILER=clang++ -DCMAKE_INSTALL_PREFIX=\"/opt/libcxx_tsan\" \"../llvm-project-llvmorg-11.0.1/llvm\"\n628: ninja install-cxx install-cxxabi\n629: \n630: rm -rf /opt/libcxx_tsan/include\n631: ```\n632: \n633: Generate local_tsan.bazelrc containing bazel configuration for tsan tests:\n634: \n635: ```\n636: bazel/setup_local_tsan.sh </path/to/instrumented/libc++/home>\n637: \n638: ```\n639: \n640: To execute TSAN tests using the local instrumented libc++ library pass `--config=local-tsan` to bazel:\n641: \n642: ```\n643: bazel test --config=local-tsan //test/...\n644: ```\n645: \n646: For [memory sanitizer (MSAN)](https://github.com/google/sanitizers/wiki/MemorySanitizer) testing,\n647: it has to be run under the docker sandbox which comes with MSAN instrumented libc++:\n648: \n649: ```\n650: bazel test -c dbg --config=docker-msan //test/...\n651: ```\n652: \n653: To run the sanitizers on OS X, prefix `macos-` to the config option, e.g.:\n654: \n655: ```\n656: bazel test -c dbg --config=macos-asan //test/...\n657: ```\n658: \n659: ## Log Verbosity\n660: \n661: Log verbosity is controlled at runtime in all builds.\n662: \n663: To obtain `nghttp2` traces, you can set `ENVOY_NGHTTP2_TRACE` in the environment for enhanced\n664: logging at `-l trace`. For example, in tests:\n665: \n666: ```\n667: bazel test //test/integration:protocol_integration_test --test_output=streamed \\\n668:   --test_arg=\"-l trace\" --test_env=\"ENVOY_NGHTTP2_TRACE=\"\n669: ```\n670: \n671: Similarly, `QUICHE` verbose logs can be enabled by setting `ENVOY_QUICHE_VERBOSITY=n` in the\n672: environment where `n` is the desired verbosity level (e.g.\n673: `--test_env=\"ENVOY_QUICHE_VERBOSITY=2\"`.\n674: \n675: ## Disabling optional features\n676: \n677: The following optional features can be disabled on the Bazel build command-line:\n678: \n679: * Hot restart with `--define hot_restart=disabled`\n680: * Google C++ gRPC client with `--define google_grpc=disabled`\n681: * Backtracing on signals with `--define signal_trace=disabled`\n682: * Active stream state dump on signals with `--define signal_trace=disabled` or `--define disable_object_dump_on_signal_trace=disabled`\n683: * tcmalloc with `--define tcmalloc=disabled`. Also you can choose Gperftools' implementation of\n684:   tcmalloc with `--define tcmalloc=gperftools` which is the default for builds other than x86_64 and aarch64.\n685: * deprecated features with `--define deprecated_features=disabled`\n686: * http3/quic with `--//bazel:http3=False`\n687: * autolinking libraries with `--define=library_autolink=disabled`\n688: * admin HTML home page with `--define=admin_html=disabled`\n689: * admin functionality with `--define=admin_functionality=disabled`\n690: * static extension registration with `--define=static_extension_registration=disabled`\n691: * spdlogging functionality with `--define=enable_logging=disabled`\n692: \n693: ## Enabling optional features\n694: \n695: The following optional features can be enabled on the Bazel build command-line:\n696: \n697: * Exported symbols during linking with `--define exported_symbols=enabled`.\n698:   This config will exports all symbols and results in larger binary size. If partial symbols export\n699:   is required and target platform is Linux, then `bazel/exported_symbols.txt` can be used to land it.\n700: * Perf annotation with `--define perf_annotation=enabled` (see\n701:   source/common/common/perf_annotation.h for details).\n702: * BoringSSL can be built in a FIPS-compliant mode with `--define boringssl=fips`\n703:   (see [FIPS 140-2](https://www.envoyproxy.io/docs/envoy/latest/intro/arch_overview/security/ssl#fips-140-2) for details).\n704: * ASSERT() can be configured to log failures and increment a stat counter in a release build with\n705:   `--define log_fast_debug_assert_in_release=enabled`. SLOW_ASSERT()s can be included with `--define log_debug_assert_in_release=enabled`. The default behavior is to compile all debug assertions out of\n706:   release builds so that the condition is not evaluated. This option has no effect in debug builds.\n707: * memory-debugging (scribbling over memory after allocation and before freeing) with\n708:   `--define tcmalloc=debug`. Note this option cannot be used with FIPS-compliant mode BoringSSL and\n709:   tcmalloc is built from the sources of Gperftools.\n710: * Default [path normalization](https://github.com/envoyproxy/envoy/issues/6435) with\n711:   `--define path_normalization_by_default=true`. Note this still could be disable by explicit xDS config.\n712: * Manual stamping via VersionInfo with `--define manual_stamp=manual_stamp`.\n713:   This is needed if the `version_info_lib` is compiled via a non-binary bazel rules, e.g `envoy_cc_library`.\n714:   Otherwise, the linker will fail to resolve symbols that are included via the `linktamp` rule, which is only available to binary targets.\n715:   This is being tracked as a feature in: https://github.com/envoyproxy/envoy/issues/6859.\n716: * Process logging for Android applications can be enabled with `--define logger=android`.\n717: * Excluding assertions for known issues with `--define disable_known_issue_asserts=true`.\n718:   A KNOWN_ISSUE_ASSERT is an assertion that should pass (like all assertions), but sometimes fails for some as-yet unidentified or unresolved reason. Because it is known to potentially fail, it can be compiled out even when DEBUG is true, when this flag is set. This allows Envoy to be run in production with assertions generally enabled, without crashing for known issues. KNOWN_ISSUE_ASSERT should only be used for newly-discovered issues that represent benign violations of expectations.\n719: * Envoy can be linked to [`zlib-ng`](https://github.com/zlib-ng/zlib-ng) instead of\n720:   [`zlib`](https://zlib.net) with `--define zlib=ng`.\n721: \n722: ## Enabling and disabling extensions\n723: \n724: Envoy uses a modular build which allows extensions to be removed if they are not needed or desired.\n725: Extensions that can be removed are contained in\n726: [extensions_build_config.bzl](../source/extensions/extensions_build_config.bzl). Contrib build\n727: extensions are contained in [contrib_build_config.bzl](../contrib/contrib_build_config.bzl). Note\n728: that contrib extensions are only included by default when building the contrib executable and in\n729: the default contrib images pushed to Docker Hub.\n730: \n731: The extensions disabled by default can be enabled by adding the following parameter to Bazel, for example to enable\n732: `envoy.filters.http.kill_request` extension, add `--//source/extensions/filters/http/kill_request:enabled`.\n733: The extensions enabled by default can be disabled by adding the following parameter to Bazel, for example to disable\n734: `envoy.wasm.runtime.v8` extension, add `--//source/extensions/wasm_runtime/v8:enabled=false`.\n735: Note not all extensions can be disabled.\n736: \n737: To enable a specific WebAssembly (Wasm) engine, you'll need to pass `--define wasm=[wasm_engine]`, e.g. `--define wasm=wasmtime` to enable the [wasmtime](https://wasmtime.dev/) engine. Supported engines are:\n738: \n739: * `v8` (the default included engine)\n740: * `wamr`\n741: * `wasmtime`\n742: \n743: If you're building from a custom build repository, the parameters need to prefixed with `@envoy`, for example\n744: `--@envoy//source/extensions/filters/http/kill_request:enabled`.\n745: \n746: You may persist those options in `user.bazelrc` in Envoy repo or your `.bazelrc`.\n747: \n748: Contrib extensions can be enabled and disabled similarly to above when building the contrib\n749: executable. For example:\n750: \n751: `bazel build //contrib/exe:envoy-static --//contrib/squash/filters/http/source:enabled=false`\n752: \n753: Will disable the squash extension when building the contrib executable.\n754: \n755: ## Customize extension build config\n756: \n757: You can also use the following procedure to customize the extensions for your build:\n758: \n759: * The Envoy build assumes that a Bazel repository named `@envoy_build_config` exists which\n760:   contains the file `@envoy_build_config//:extensions_build_config.bzl`. In the default build,\n761:   a synthetic repository is created containing [extensions_build_config.bzl](../source/extensions/extensions_build_config.bzl).\n762: * Start by creating a new Bazel workspace somewhere in the filesystem that your build can access.\n763:   This workspace should contain:\n764:   * Empty WORKSPACE file.\n765:   * Empty BUILD file.\n766:   * A copy of [extensions_build_config.bzl](../source/extensions/extensions_build_config.bzl).\n767:   * Comment out any extensions that you don't want to build in your file copy.\n768: \n769: To have your local build use your overridden configuration repository there are two options:\n770: \n771: 1. Use the [`--override_repository`](https://docs.bazel.build/versions/master/command-line-reference.html)\n772:    CLI option to override the `@envoy_build_config` repo.\n773: 2. Use the following snippet in your WORKSPACE before you load the Envoy repository. E.g.,\n774: \n775: ```\n776: workspace(name = \"envoy_filter_example\")\n777: \n778: local_repository(\n779:     name = \"envoy_build_config\",\n780:     # Relative paths are also supported.\n781:     path = \"/somewhere/on/filesystem/envoy_build_config\",\n782: )\n783: \n784: local_repository(\n785:     name = \"envoy\",\n786:     # Relative paths are also supported.\n787:     path = \"/somewhere/on/filesystem/envoy\",\n788: )\n789: \n790: ...\n791: ```\n792: \n793: When performing custom builds, it is acceptable to include contrib extensions as well. This can\n794: be done by including the desired Bazel paths from [contrib_build_config.bzl](../contrib/contrib_build_config.bzl)\n795: into the overridden `extensions_build_config.bzl`. (There is no need to specifically perform\n796: a contrib build to include a contrib extension.)\n797: \n798: ## Extra extensions\n799: \n800: If you are building your own Envoy extensions or custom Envoy builds and encounter visibility\n801: problems with, you may need to adjust the default visibility rules to be public,\n802: as documented in\n803: [extensions_build_config.bzl](../source/extensions/extensions_build_config.bzl).\n804: See the instructions above about how to create your own custom version of\n805: [extensions_build_config.bzl](../source/extensions/extensions_build_config.bzl).\n806: \n807: # Release builds\n808: \n809: Release builds should be built in `opt` mode, processed with `strip` and have a\n810: `.note.gnu.build-id` section with the Git SHA1 at which the build took place.\n811: They should also ignore any local `.bazelrc` for reproducibility. This can be\n812: achieved with:\n813: \n814: ```\n815: bazel --bazelrc=/dev/null build -c opt envoy.stripped\n816: ```\n817: \n818: One caveat to note is that the Git SHA1 is truncated to 16 bytes today as a\n819: result of the workaround in place for\n820: https://github.com/bazelbuild/bazel/issues/2805.\n821: \n822: # Coverage builds\n823: \n824: To generate coverage results, make sure you are using a Clang toolchain and have `llvm-cov` and\n825: `llvm-profdata` in your `PATH`. Then run:\n826: \n827: ```\n828: test/run_envoy_bazel_coverage.sh\n829: ```\n830: \n831: **Note** that it is important to ensure that the versions of `clang`, `llvm-cov` and `llvm-profdata`\n832: are consistent and that they match the most recent Clang/LLVM toolchain version in use by Envoy (see\n833: the [build container\n834: toolchain](https://github.com/envoyproxy/envoy-build-tools/blob/main/build_container/build_container_ubuntu.sh) for reference).\n835: \n836: The summary results are printed to the standard output and the full coverage\n837: report is available in `generated/coverage/coverage.html`.\n838: \n839: To generate coverage results for fuzz targets, use the `FUZZ_COVERAGE` environment variable, e.g.:\n840: ```\n841: FUZZ_COVERAGE=true VALIDATE_COVERAGE=false test/run_envoy_bazel_coverage.sh\n842: ```\n843: This generates a coverage report for fuzz targets after running the target for one minute against fuzzing engine libfuzzer using its coprus as initial seed inputs. The full coverage report will be available in `generated/fuzz_coverage/coverage.html`.\n844: \n845: Coverage for every PR is available in Circle in the \"artifacts\" tab of the coverage job. You will\n846: need to navigate down and open \"coverage.html\" but then you can navigate per normal. NOTE: We\n847: have seen some issues with seeing the artifacts tab. If you can't see it, log out of Circle, and\n848: then log back in and it should start working.\n849: \n850: The latest coverage report for main is available\n851: [here](https://storage.googleapis.com/envoy-postsubmit/main/coverage/index.html). The latest fuzz coverage report for main is available [here](https://storage.googleapis.com/envoy-postsubmit/main/fuzz_coverage/index.html).\n852: \n853: It's also possible to specialize the coverage build to a specified test or test dir. This is useful\n854: when doing things like exploring the coverage of a fuzzer over its corpus. This can be done by\n855: passing coverage targets as the command-line arguments and using the `VALIDATE_COVERAGE` environment\n856: variable, e.g. for a fuzz test:\n857: \n858: ```\n859: FUZZ_COVERAGE=true VALIDATE_COVERAGE=false test/run_envoy_bazel_coverage.sh //test/common/common:base64_fuzz_test\n860: ```\n861: \n862: # Cleaning the build and test artifacts\n863: \n864: `bazel clean` will nuke all the build/test artifacts from the Bazel cache for\n865: Envoy proper. To remove the artifacts for the external dependencies run\n866: `bazel clean --expunge`.\n867: \n868: If something goes really wrong and none of the above work to resolve a stale build issue, you can\n869: always remove your Bazel cache completely. It is likely located in `~/.cache/bazel`.\n870: \n871: # Adding or maintaining Envoy build rules\n872: \n873: See the [developer guide for writing Envoy Bazel rules](DEVELOPER.md).\n874: \n875: # Bazel performance on (virtual) machines with low resources\n876: \n877: If the (virtual) machine that is performing the build is low on memory or CPU\n878: resources, you can override Bazel's default job parallelism determination with\n879: `--jobs=N` to restrict the build to at most `N` simultaneous jobs, e.g.:\n880: \n881: ```\n882: bazel build --jobs=2 envoy\n883: ```\n884: \n885: # Debugging the Bazel build\n886: \n887: When trying to understand what Bazel is doing, the `-s` and `--explain` options\n888: are useful. To have Bazel provide verbose output on which commands it is executing:\n889: \n890: ```\n891: bazel build -s envoy\n892: ```\n893: \n894: To have Bazel emit to a text file the rationale for rebuilding a target:\n895: \n896: ```\n897: bazel build --explain=file.txt envoy\n898: ```\n899: \n900: To get more verbose explanations:\n901: \n902: ```\n903: bazel build --explain=file.txt --verbose_explanations envoy\n904: ```\n905: \n906: # Resolving paths in bazel build output\n907: \n908: Sometimes it's useful to see real system paths in bazel error message output (vs. symbolic links).\n909: `tools/path_fix.sh` is provided to help with this. See the comments in that file.\n910: \n911: # Compilation database\n912: \n913: Run `tools/gen_compilation_database.py` to generate\n914: a [JSON Compilation Database](https://clang.llvm.org/docs/JSONCompilationDatabase.html). This could be used\n915: with any tools (e.g. clang-tidy) compatible with the format. It is recommended to run this script\n916: with `TEST_TMPDIR` set, so the Bazel artifacts doesn't get cleaned up in next `bazel build` or `bazel test`.\n917: \n918: The compilation database could also be used to setup editors with cross reference, code completion.\n919: For example, you can use [You Complete Me](https://valloric.github.io/YouCompleteMe/) or\n920: [clangd](https://clangd.llvm.org/) with supported editors.\n921: \n922: This requires Python 3.8.0+, download from [here](https://www.python.org/downloads/) if you do not have it installed already.\n923: \n924: Use the following command to prepare a compilation database:\n925: \n926: ```\n927: TEST_TMPDIR=/tmp tools/gen_compilation_database.py\n928: ```\n929: \n930: \n931: # Running format linting without docker\n932: \n933: Note that if you run the `check_spelling.py` script you will need to have `aspell` installed.\n934: \n935: You can run clang-format directly, without docker:\n936: \n937: ```shell\n938: bazel run //tools/code_format:check_format -- check\n939: ./tools/spelling/check_spelling_pedantic.py check\n940: bazel run //tools/code_format:check_format -- fix\n941: ./tools/spelling/check_spelling_pedantic.py fix\n942: ```\n943: \n944: # Advanced caching setup\n945: \n946: Setting up an HTTP cache for Bazel output helps optimize Bazel performance and resource usage when\n947: using multiple compilation modes or multiple trees.\n948: \n949: ## Setup local cache\n950: \n951: You may use any [Remote Caching](https://docs.bazel.build/versions/master/remote-caching.html) backend\n952: as an alternative to this.\n953: \n954: This requires Go 1.11+, follow the [instructions](https://golang.org/doc/install#install) to install\n955: if you don't have one. To start the cache, run the following from the root of the Envoy repository (or anywhere else\n956: that the Go toolchain can find the necessary dependencies):\n957: \n958: ```\n959: go run github.com/buchgr/bazel-remote --dir ${HOME}/bazel_cache --host 127.0.0.1 --port 28080 --max_size 64\n960: ```\n961: \n962: See [Bazel remote cache](https://github.com/buchgr/bazel-remote) for more information on the parameters.\n963: The command above will setup a maximum 64 GiB cache at `~/bazel_cache` on port 28080. You might\n964: want to setup a larger cache if you run ASAN builds.\n965: \n966: NOTE: Using docker to run remote cache server described in remote cache docs will likely have\n967: slower cache performance on macOS due to slow disk performance on Docker for Mac.\n968: \n969: Adding the following parameter to Bazel everytime or persist them in `.bazelrc`.\n970: \n971: ```\n972: --remote_cache=http://127.0.0.1:28080/\n973: ```\n974: ","url":"https://sourcegraph.sourcegraph.com/github.com/sg-evals/envoy--v1.32.1@b35dd17bea856e19fc4e65fb05e68170841d3726/-/blob/bazel/README.md"}}}

The top level directories\\n5: are:\\n6: \\n7: * [.azure-pipelines/](.azure-pipelines/): Configuration for\\n8: [Azure Pipelines](https://azure.microsoft.com/en-us/services/devops/pipelines/).\\n9: * [api/](api/): Envoy data plane API.\\n10: * [bazel/](bazel/): Configuration for Envoy's use of [Bazel](https://bazel.build/).\\n11: * [ci/](ci/): Scripts used both during CI as well as to build Docker containers.\\n12: * [configs/](configs/): Example Envoy configurations.\\n13: * [docs/](docs/): End user facing Envoy proxy and data plane API documentation as well as scripts\\n14:   for publishing final docs during releases.\\n15: * [examples/](examples/): Larger Envoy examples using Docker and Docker Compose.\\n16: * [envoy/](envoy/): \\\"Public\\\" interface headers for \\\"core\\\" Envoy. In general,\\n17:   these are almost entirely 100% abstract classes. There are a few cases of not-abstract classes in\\n18:   the \\\"public\\\" headers, typically for performance reasons. Note that \\\"core\\\" includes some\\n19:   \\\"extensions\\\" such as the HTTP connection manager filter and associated functionality which are\\n20:   so fundamental to Envoy that they will likely never be optional from a compilation perspective.\\n21: * [restarter/](restarter/): Envoy's hot restart wrapper Python script.\\n22: * [security/](security/): Some templates for reporting security issues of Envoy. Historical security issues can also be found here.\\n23: * [source/](source/): Source code for core Envoy as well as extensions. The layout of this directory\\n24:   is discussed in further detail below.\\n25: * [support/](support/): Development support scripts (pre-commit Git hooks, etc.)\\n26: * [test/](test/): Test code for core Envoy as well as extensions. The layout of this directory is\\n27:   discussed in further detail below.\\n28: * [tools/](tools/): Miscellaneous tools that have not found a home somewhere else.\\n29: \\n30: ## [source/](source/)\\n31: \\n32: * [common/](source/common/): Core Envoy code (not specific to extensions) that is also not\\n33:   specific to a standalone server implementation. I.e., this is the code that could be used if Envoy\\n34:   were eventually embedded as a library.\\n35: * [docs/](source/docs/): Miscellaneous developer/design documentation that is not relevant for\\n36:   the public user documentation.\\n37: * [exe/](source/exe/): Code specific to building the final production Envoy server binary. This is\\n38:   the only code that is not shared by integration and unit tests.\\n39: * [extensions/](source/extensions/): Extensions to the core Envoy code. The layout of this\\n40:   directory is discussed in further detail below.\\n41: * [server/](source/server/): Code specific to running Envoy as a standalone server. E.g,\\n42:   configuration, server startup, workers, etc. Over time, the line between `common/` and `server/`\\n43:   has become somewhat blurred. Use best judgment as to where to place something.\\n44: \\n45: ## [test/](test/)\\n46: \\n47: Not every directory within test is described below, but a few highlights:\\n48: \\n49: * Unit tests are found in directories matching their [source/](source/) equivalents. E.g.,\\n50:   [common/](test/common/), [exe/](test/exe/), and [server/](test/server/).\\n51: * Extension unit tests also match their source equivalents in [extensions/](test/extensions/).\\n52: * [integration/](test/integration/) holds end-to-end integration tests using roughly the real\\n53:   Envoy server code, fake downstream clients, and fake upstream servers. Integration tests also\\n54:   test some of the extensions found in the repository. Note that in the future, we would like to\\n55:   allow integration tests that are specific to extensions and are not required for covering\\n56:   \\\"core\\\" Envoy functionality. Those integration tests will likely end up in the\\n57:   [extensions/](test/extensions/) directory but further work and thinking is required before\\n58:   we get to that point.\\n59: * [mocks/](test/mocks/) contains mock implementations of all of the core Envoy interfaces found in\\n60:   [include/](include/).\\n61: * Other directories include tooling used for configuration testing, coverage testing, fuzz testing,\\n62:   common test code, etc.\\n63: \\n64: ## [source/extensions](source/extensions/) layout\\n65: \\n66: We maintain a very specific code and namespace layout for extensions. This aids in discovering\\n67: code/extensions, and allows us specify extension owners in [CODEOWNERS](CODEOWNERS).\\n68: \\n69: * All extensions are either registered in [all_extensions.bzl](source/extensions/all_extensions.bzl)\\n70:   or [extensions_build_config.bzl](source/extensions/extensions_build_config.bzl). The former is\\n71:   for extensions that cannot be removed from the primary Envoy build. The latter is for extensions\\n72:   that can be removed on a site specific basis. See [bazel/README.md](bazel/README.md) for how to\\n73:   compile out extensions on a site specific basis. Note that by default extensions should be\\n74:   removable from the build unless there is a very good reason.\\n75: * These are the top level extension directories and associated namespaces:\\n76:   * [access_loggers/](/source/extensions/access_loggers): Access log implementations which use\\n77:     the `Envoy::Extensions::AccessLoggers` namespace.\\n78:   * [bootstrap/](/source/extensions/bootstrap): Bootstrap extensions which use\\n79:     the `Envoy::Extensions::Bootstrap` namespace.\\n80:   * [clusters/](/source/extensions/clusters): Cluster extensions which use the\\n81:     `Envoy::Extensions::Clusters` namespace.\\n82:   * [compression/](/source/extensions/compression): Compression extensions\\n83:     which use `Envoy::Extensions::Compression` namespace.\\n84:   * [fatal_actions/](/source/extensions/fatal_actions): Fatal Action extensions\\n85:     which use the `Envoy::Extensions::FatalActions` namespace.\\n86:   * [filters/http/](/source/extensions/filters/http): HTTP L7 filters which use the\\n87:     `Envoy::Extensions::HttpFilters` namespace.\\n88:   * [filters/listener/](/source/extensions/filters/listener): Listener filters which use the\\n89:     `Envoy::Extensions::ListenerFilters` namespace.\\n90:   * [filters/network/](/source/extensions/filters/network): L4 network filters which use the\\n91:     `Envoy::Extensions::NetworkFilters` namespace.\\n92:   * [formatters/](/source/extensions/formatters): Access log formatters which use the\\n93:     `Envoy::Extensions::Formatters` namespace.\\n94:   * [grpc_credentials/](/source/extensions/grpc_credentials): Custom gRPC credentials which use the\\n95:     `Envoy::Extensions::GrpcCredentials` namespace.\\n96:   * [health_checker/](/source/extensions/health_checker): Custom health checkers which use the\\n97:     `Envoy::Extensions::HealthCheckers` namespace.\\n98:   * [internal_redirect/](/source/extensions/internal_redirect): Internal Redirect\\n99:     extensions which use the `Envoy::Extensions::InternalRedirect` namespace.\\n100:   * [quic_listeners/](/source/extensions/quic_listeners): QUIC extensions which\\n101:     use the `Envoy::Quic` namespace.\\n102:   * [resource_monitors/](/source/extensions/resource_monitors): Resource monitor\\n103:     extensions which use the `Envoy::Extensions::ResourceMonitors` namespace.\\n104:   * [retry/](/source/extensions/retry): Retry extensions which use the\\n105:     `Envoy::Extensions::Retry` namespace.\\n106:   * [stat_sinks/](/source/extensions/stat_sinks): Stat sink implementations which use the\\n107:     `Envoy::Extensions::StatSinks` namespace.\\n108:   * [tracers/](/source/extensions/tracers): Tracers which use the\\n109:     `Envoy::Extensions::Tracers` namespace.\\n110:   * [transport_sockets/](/source/extensions/transport_sockets): Transport socket implementations\\n111:     which use the `Envoy::Extensions::TransportSockets` namespace.\\n112:   * [upstreams/](/source/extensions/upstreams): Upstream extensions use the\\n113:     `Envoy::Extensions::Upstreams` namespace.\\n114:   * [watchdog/](/source/extensions/watchdog): Watchdog extensions use the\\n115:     `Envoy::Extensions::Watchdog` namespace.\\n116:   * [rate_limit_descriptors/](/source/extensions/rate_limit_descriptors): Rate limit\\n117:     descriptor extensions use the `Envoy::Extensions::RateLimitDescriptors`\\n118:     namespace.\\n119: * Each extension is contained wholly in its own namespace. E.g.,\\n120:   `Envoy::Extensions::NetworkFilters::Echo`.\\n121: * Common code that is used by multiple extensions should be in a `common/` directory as close to\\n122:   the extensions as possible. E.g., [filters/common/](/source/extensions/filters/common) for common\\n123:   code that is used by both HTTP and network filters. Common code used only by two HTTP filters\\n124:   would be found in `filters/http/common/`. Common code should be placed in a common namespace.\\n125:   E.g., `Envoy::Extensions::Filters::Common`.\\n126: \\n127: ## [contrib](contrib/) layout\\n128: \\n129: This directory contains contrib extensions. This is similar to the\\n133:   `envoy-static` target but also includes all contrib extensions, and is used to produce the\\n134:   contrib image targets.\\n135: * [contrib/...](contrib/): The rest of this directory mirrors the [source/extensions](source/extensions/)\\n136:   layout. The top level directories\n5: are:\n6: \n7: * [.azure-pipelines/](.azure-pipelines/): Configuration for\n8: [Azure Pipelines](https://azure.microsoft.com/en-us/services/devops/pipelines/).\n9: * [api/](api/): Envoy data plane API.\n10: * [bazel/](bazel/): Configuration for Envoy's use of [Bazel](https://bazel.build/).\n11: * [ci/](ci/): Scripts used both during CI as well as to build Docker containers.\n12: * [configs/](configs/): Example Envoy configurations.\n13: * [docs/](docs/): End user facing Envoy proxy and data plane API documentation as well as scripts\n14:   for publishing final docs during releases.\n15: * [examples/](examples/): Larger Envoy examples using Docker and Docker Compose.\n16: * [envoy/](envoy/): \"Public\" interface headers for \"core\" Envoy. In general,\n17:   these are almost entirely 100% abstract classes. There are a few cases of not-abstract classes in\n18:   the \"public\" headers, typically for performance reasons. Note that \"core\" includes some\n19:   \"extensions\" such as the HTTP connection manager filter and associated functionality which are\n20:   so fundamental to Envoy that they will likely never be optional from a compilation perspective.\n21: * [restarter/](restarter/): Envoy's hot restart wrapper Python script.\n22: * [security/](security/): Some templates for reporting security issues of Envoy. Historical security issues can also be found here.\n23: * [source/](source/): Source code for core Envoy as well as extensions. The layout of this directory\n24:   is discussed in further detail below.\n25: * [support/](support/): Development support scripts (pre-commit Git hooks, etc.)\n26: * [test/](test/): Test code for core Envoy as well as extensions. The layout of this directory is\n27:   discussed in further detail below.\n28: * [tools/](tools/): Miscellaneous tools that have not found a home somewhere else.\n29: \n30: ## [source/](source/)\n31: \n32: * [common/](source/common/): Core Envoy code (not specific to extensions) that is also not\n33:   specific to a standalone server implementation. I.e., this is the code that could be used if Envoy\n34:   were eventually embedded as a library.\n35: * [docs/](source/docs/): Miscellaneous developer/design documentation that is not relevant for\n36:   the public user documentation.\n37: * [exe/](source/exe/): Code specific to building the final production Envoy server binary. This is\n38:   the only code that is not shared by integration and unit tests.\n39: * [extensions/](source/extensions/): Extensions to the core Envoy code. The layout of this\n40:   directory is discussed in further detail below.\n41: * [server/](source/server/): Code specific to running Envoy as a standalone server. E.g,\n42:   configuration, server startup, workers, etc. Over time, the line between `common/` and `server/`\n43:   has become somewhat blurred. Use best judgment as to where to place something.\n44: \n45: ## [test/](test/)\n46: \n47: Not every directory within test is described below, but a few highlights:\n48: \n49: * Unit tests are found in directories matching their [source/](source/) equivalents.
