Until further notice, Windows\n32: builds are excluded from Envoy CI, as well as the Envoy release and security processes.\n33: \n34: The Windows 2019 based Envoy Docker image at [`envoyproxy/envoy-build-windows2019:<hash>`](https://hub.docker.com/r/envoyproxy/envoy-build-windows2019/)\n35: is used for CI checks, where `<hash>` is specified in [`envoy_build_sha.sh`](https://github.com/envoyproxy/envoy/blob/main/ci/envoy_build_sha.sh).\n36: Developers may work with the most recent `envoyproxy/envoy-build-windows2019` image to provide a self-contained environment for building Envoy binaries and\n37: running tests that reflects the latest built Windows 2019 Envoy image.\n38: \n39: # Build image base and compiler versions\n40: \n41: Currently there are three build images for Linux and one for Windows:\n42: \n43: * `envoyproxy/envoy-build` &mdash; alias to `envoyproxy/envoy-build-ubuntu`.\n44: * `envoyproxy/envoy-build-ubuntu` &mdash; based on Ubuntu 20.04 (Focal) with GCC 9 and Clang 14 compiler.\n45: * `envoyproxy/envoy-build-centos` &mdash; based on CentOS 7 with GCC 9 and Clang 14 compiler, this image is experimental and not well tested.\n46: * `envoyproxy/envoy-build-windows2019` &mdash; based on Windows ltsc2019 with VS 2019 Build Tools, as well as LLVM.\n47: \n48: The source for these images is located in the [envoyproxy/envoy-build-tools](https://github.com/envoyproxy/envoy-build-tools)\n49: repository.\n50: \n51: We use the Clang compiler for all Linux CI runs with tests. We have an additional Linux CI run with GCC which builds binary only.\n52: \n53: # C++ standard library\n54: \n55: As of November 2019 after [#8859](https://github.com/envoyproxy/envoy/pull/8859) the official released binary is\n56: [linked against libc++ on Linux](https://github.com/envoyproxy/envoy/blob/main/bazel/README.md#linking-against-libc-on-linux).\n57: To override the C++ standard library in your build, set environment variable `ENVOY_STDLIB` to `libstdc++` or `libc++` and\n58: run `./ci/do_ci.sh` as described below.\n59: \n60: # Building and running tests as a developer\n61: \n62: The `./ci/run_envoy_docker.sh` script can be used to set up a Docker container on Linux and Windows\n63: to build an Envoy static binary and run tests.\n64: \n65: The build image defaults to `envoyproxy/envoy-build-ubuntu` on Linux and\n66: `envoyproxy/envoy-build-windows2019` on Windows, but you can choose build image by setting\n67: `IMAGE_NAME` in the environment.\n68: \n69: In case your setup is behind a proxy, set `http_proxy` and `https_proxy` to the proxy servers before\n70: invoking the build.\n71: \n72: ```bash\n73: IMAGE_NAME=envoyproxy/envoy-build-ubuntu http_proxy=http://proxy.foo.com:8080 https_proxy=http://proxy.bar.com:8080 ./ci/run_envoy_docker.sh <build_script_args>\n74: ```\n75: \n76: Besides `http_proxy` and `https_proxy`, maybe you need to set `go_proxy` to replace the default GOPROXY in China.\n77: \n78: ```bash\n79: IMAGE_NAME=envoyproxy/envoy-build-ubuntu go_proxy=https://goproxy.cn,direct http_proxy=http://proxy.foo.com:8080 https_proxy=http://proxy.bar.com:8080 ./ci/run_envoy_docker.sh <build_script_args>\n80: ```\n81: \n82: To force the Envoy build image to be refreshed by Docker you can set `ENVOY_DOCKER_PULL=true`.\n83: \n84: ```bash\n85: ENVOY_DOCKER_PULL=true ./ci/run_envoy_docker.sh <build_script_args>\n86: ```\n87: \n88: \n89: # Generating compile commands\n90: \n91: The `./ci/do_ci.sh` script provides a CI target that generates compile commands for clangd or other tools.\n92: \n93: ```bash\n94: ENVOY_GEN_COMPDB_OPTIONS=\"--vscode --exclude_contrib\" ./ci/do_ci.sh refresh_compdb\n95: ```\n96: \n97: ## On Linux\n98: \n99: An example basic invocation to build a developer version of the Envoy static binary (using the Bazel `fastbuild` type) is:\n100: \n101: ```bash\n102: ./ci/run_envoy_docker.sh './ci/do_ci.sh dev'\n103: ```\n104: \n105: The Envoy binary can be found in `/tmp/envoy-docker-build/envoy/source/exe/envoy-fastbuild` on the Docker host. You\n106: can control this by setting `ENVOY_DOCKER_BUILD_DIR` in the environment, e.g. to\n107: generate the binary in `~/build/envoy/source/exe/envoy-fastbuild` you can run:\n108: \n109: ```bash\n110: ENVOY_DOCKER_BUILD_DIR=~/build ./ci/run_envoy_docker.sh './ci/do_ci.sh dev'\n111: ```\n112: \n113: For a release version of the Envoy binary you can run:\n114: \n115: ```bash\n116: ./ci/run_envoy_docker.sh './ci/do_ci.sh release.server_only'\n117: ```\n118: \n119: The build artifact can be found in `/tmp/envoy-docker-build/envoy/source/exe/envoy` (or wherever\n120: `$ENVOY_DOCKER_BUILD_DIR` points).\n121: \n122: To enable the previous behavior of the `release.server_only` target where the final binary was copied to a tar.gz file\n123: (e.g. envoy-binary.tar.gz), you can run:\n124: \n125:   ```bash\n126:   ./ci/run_envoy_docker.sh './ci/do_ci.sh release.server_only.binary'\n127:   ```\n128: \n129: For a debug version of the Envoy binary you can run:\n130: \n131: ```bash\n132: ./ci/run_envoy_docker.sh './ci/do_ci.sh debug.server_only'\n133: ```\n134: \n135: The build artifact can be found in `/tmp/envoy-docker-build/envoy/source/exe/envoy-debug` (or wherever\n136: `$ENVOY_DOCKER_BUILD_DIR` points).\n137: \n138: To leverage a [bazel remote cache](https://github.com/envoyproxy/envoy/tree/main/bazel#advanced-caching-setup):\n139: 1. add bazel options like `--remote_cache` and/or `--remote_cache_header` to a `.bazelrc` file, such as `user.bazelrc`. For example\n140: \n141: ```bash\n142: build:my-remote-cache --remote_cache=grpcs://remotecache.googleapis.com\n143: build:my-remote-cache --remote_cache_header=Authorization=\"Bearer <token>\"\n144: ```\n145: \n146: 2. specify the config in the `BAZEL_BUILD_EXTRA_OPTIONS` environment variable. Run\n147: \n148: ```bash\n149: export BAZEL_BUILD_EXTRA_OPTIONS=--config=my-remote-cache\n150: ```\n151: \n152: The `./ci/run_envoy_docker.sh './ci/do_ci.sh <TARGET>'` targets are:\n153: \n154: * `api` &mdash; build and run API tests under `-c fastbuild` with clang.\n155: * `asan` &mdash; build and run tests under `-c dbg --config=clang-asan` with clang.\n156: * `asan <test>` &mdash; build and run a specified test or test dir under `-c dbg --config=clang-asan` with clang.\n157: * `debug` &mdash; build Envoy static binary and run tests under `-c dbg`.\n158: * `debug <test>` &mdash; build Envoy static binary and run a specified test or test dir under `-c dbg`.\n159: * `debug.server_only` &mdash; build Envoy static binary under `-c dbg`.\n160: * `docker` &mdash; build Docker images, expects `release` or `release.server_only` to have been run first.\n161: * `dev` &mdash; build Envoy static binary and run tests under `-c fastbuild` with clang.\n162: * `dev <test>` &mdash; build Envoy static binary and run a specified test or test dir under `-c fastbuild` with clang.\n163: * `dev.contrib` &mdash; build Envoy static binary with contrib and run tests under `-c fastbuild` with clang.\n164: * `dev.contrib <test>` &mdash; build Envoy static binary with contrib and run a specified test or test dir under `-c fastbuild` with clang.\n165: * `release` &mdash; build Envoy static binary and run tests under `-c opt` with clang.\n166: * `release <test>` &mdash; build Envoy static binaries and run a specified test or test dir under `-c opt` with clang.\n167: * `release.server_only` &mdash; build Envoy static binaries under `-c opt` with clang.\n168: * `sizeopt` &mdash; build Envoy static binary and run tests under `-c opt --config=sizeopt` with clang.\n169: * `sizeopt <test>` &mdash; build Envoy static binary and run a specified test or test dir under `-c opt --config=sizeopt` with clang.\n170: * `sizeopt.server_only` &mdash; build Envoy static binary under `-c opt --config=sizeopt` with clang.\n171: * `coverage` &mdash; build and run tests under `-c dbg` with gcc, generating coverage information in `$ENVOY_DOCKER_BUILD_DIR/envoy/generated/coverage/coverage.html`.\n172: * `coverage <test>` &mdash; build and run a specified test or test dir under `-c dbg` with gcc, generating coverage information in `$ENVOY_DOCKER_BUILD_DIR/envoy/generated/coverage/coverage.html`. Specify `//contrib/...` to get contrib coverage.\n173: * `msan` &mdash; build and run tests under `-c dbg --config=clang-msan` with clang.\n174: * `msan <test>` &mdash; build and run a specified test or test dir under `-c dbg --config=clang-msan` with clang.\n175: * `tsan` &mdash; build and run tests under `-c dbg --config=clang-tsan` with clang.\n176: * `tsan <test>` &mdash; build and run a specified test or test dir under `-c dbg --config=clang-tsan` with clang.\n177: * `fuzz` &mdash; build and run fuzz tests under `-c dbg --config=asan-fuzzer` with clang.\n178: * `fuzz <test>` &mdash; build and run a specified fuzz test or test dir under `-c dbg --config=asan-fuzzer` with clang. If specifying a single fuzz test, must use the full target name with \"_with_libfuzzer\" for `<test>`.\n179: * `compile_time_options` &mdash; build Envoy and run tests with various compile-time options toggled to their non-default state, to ensure they still build.\n180: * `compile_time_options <test>` &mdash; build Envoy and run a specified test or test dir with various compile-time options toggled to their non-default state, to ensure they still build.\n181: * `clang_tidy <files>` &mdash; build and run clang-tidy specified source files, if no files specified, runs against the diff with the last GitHub commit.\n182: * `check_proto_format`&mdash; check configuration, formatting and build issues in API proto files.\n183: * `fix_proto_format`&mdash; fix configuration, formatting and build issues in API proto files.\n184: * `check_and_fix_proto_format` &mdash; check and fix configuration, fomatting and build issues in API proto files.\n185: * `format`&mdash; run validation, linting and formatting tools.\n186: * `docs`&mdash; build documentation tree in `generated/docs`.\n187: \n188: ## On Windows\n189: \n190: An example basic invocation to build the Envoy static binary and run tests is:\n191: \n192: ```bash\n193: ./ci/run_envoy_docker.sh './ci/windows_ci_steps.sh'\n194: ```\n195: \n196: You can pass additional command line arguments to `./ci/windows_ci_steps.sh` to list specific `bazel` arguments and build/test targets.\n197: as set environment variables to adjust your container build environment as described above.\n198: \n199: The Envoy binary can be found in `${TEMP}\\envoy-docker-build\\envoy\\source\\exe` on the Docker host. You\n200: can control this by setting `ENVOY_DOCKER_BUILD_DIR` in the environment, e.g. to\n201: generate the binary in `C:\\Users\\foo\\build\\envoy\\source\\exe` you can run:\n202: \n203: ```bash\n204: ENVOY_DOCKER_BUILD_DIR=\"C:\\Users\\foo\\build\" ./ci/run_envoy_docker.sh './ci/windows_ci_steps.sh'\n205: ```\n206: \n207: Note the quotations around the `ENVOY_DOCKER_BUILD_DIR` value to preserve the backslashes in the\n208: path.\n209: \n210: If you would like to run an interactive session to keep the build container running (to persist your local build environment), run:\n211: \n212: ```bash\n213: ./ci/run_envoy_docker.sh 'bash'\n214: ```\n215: \n216: From an interactive session, you can invoke `bazel` directly, or use the `./ci/windows_ci_steps.sh` script to build and run tests.\n217: Bazel will look for .bazelrc in the `${HOME}` path, which is mapped to the persistent path `${TEMP}\\envoy-docker-build\\` on the\n218: Docker host.\n219: \n220: # Testing changes to the build image as a developer\n221: \n222: The base build image used in the CI flows here lives in the [envoy-build-tools](https://github.com/envoyproxy/envoy-build-tools)\n223: repository. If you need to make and/or test changes to the build image, instructions to do so can be found in\n224: the [build_container](https://github.com/envoyproxy/envoy-build-tools/blob/main/build_container/README.md) folder.\n225: See the Dockerfiles and build scripts there for building a new image.\n226: \n227: # macOS Build Flow\n228: \n229: The macOS CI build is part of the [Azure Pipelines](https://dev.azure.com/cncf/envoy/_build) workflow.\n230: Dependencies are installed by the `ci/mac_ci_setup.sh` script, via [Homebrew](https://brew.sh),\n231: which is pre-installed on the [Azure Pipelines macOS image](https://github.com/actions/virtual-environments/blob/main/images/macos/macos-10.15-Readme.md).\n232: The dependencies are cached and re-installed on every build. The `ci/mac_ci_steps.sh` script executes the specific commands that\n233: build and test Envoy. See the documentation on those pages for information on the\\n7: various classes, macros, and matchers that Envoy uses from those frameworks.\\n8: \\n9: ## Integration tests\\n10: \\n11: Envoy contains an integration testing framework, for testing\\n12: downstream-Envoy-upstream communication.\\n13: [See the framework's README for more information.](https://github.com/envoyproxy/envoy/blob/main/test/integration/README.md)\\n14: \\n15: ## Custom matchers\\n16: \\n17: Envoy includes some custom Google Mock matchers to make test expectation\\n18: statements simpler to write and easier to understand.\\n19: \\n20: ### HeaderValueOf\\n21: \\n22: Tests that a HeaderMap argument contains exactly one header with the given key,\\n23: whose value satisfies the given expectation. The expectation can be a matcher,\\n24: or a string that the value should equal.\\n25: \\n26: Examples:\\n27: \\n28: ```cpp\\n29: EXPECT_THAT(response->headers(), HeaderValueOf(Headers::get().Server, \\\"envoy\\\"));\\n30: ```\\n31: \\n32: ```cpp\\n33: using testing::HasSubstr;\\n34: EXPECT_THAT(request->headers(),\\n35:             HeaderValueOf(Headers::get().AcceptEncoding, HasSubstr(\\\"gzip\\\")));\\n36: ```\\n37: \\n38: ### HttpStatusIs\\n39: \\n40: Tests that a HeaderMap argument has the provided HTTP status code. The status\\n41: code can be passed in as a string or an integer.\\n42: \\n43: Example:\\n44: \\n45: ```cpp\\n46: EXPECT_THAT(response->headers(), HttpStatusIs(\\\"200\\\"));\\n47: ```\\n48: \\n49: ### HeaderMapEqual and HeaderMapEqualRef\\n50: \\n51: `HeaderMapEqualRef` tests that two `HeaderMap` arguments are equal.\\n52: `HeaderMapEqual` is the same, but it compares two pointers to `HeaderMap`s, and\\n53: the matcher's argument must be a `HeaderMapPtr`.\\n54: \\n55: Example:\\n56: \\n57: ```cpp\\n58: EXPECT_THAT(response->headers(), HeaderMapEqualRef(expected_headers));\\n59: ```\\n60: \\n61: ### ProtoEq, ProtoEqIgnoringField, RepeatedProtoEq\\n62: \\n63: Tests equality of protobufs, with a variant that ignores the value (including\\n64: presence) of a single named field. Another variant can be used to compare two\\n65: instances of Protobuf::RepeatedPtrField element-by-element.\\n66: \\n67: Example:\\n68: \\n69: ```cpp\\n70: envoy::service::discovery::v3::DeltaDiscoveryRequest expected_request;\\n71: // (not shown: set some fields of expected_request...)\\n72: EXPECT_CALL(async_stream_, sendMessage(ProtoEqIgnoringField(expected_request, \\\"response_nonce\\\"), false));\\n73: \\n74: response->mutable_resources()->Add();\\n75: response->mutable_resources()->Add();\\n76: response->mutable_resources()->Add();\\n77: // (not shown: do something to populate those empty added items...)\\n78: EXPECT_CALL(callbacks_, onConfigUpdate(RepeatedProtoEq(response->resources()), version));\\n79: ```\\n80: \\n81: ### IsSubsetOfHeaders and IsSupersetOfHeaders\\n82: \\n83: Tests that one `HeaderMap` argument contains every header in another\\n84: `HeaderMap`.\\n85: \\n86: Examples:\\n87: \\n88: ```cpp\\n89: EXPECT_THAT(response->headers(), IsSubsetOfHeaders(allowed_headers));\\n90: EXPECT_THAT(response->headers(), IsSupersetOfHeaders(required_headers));\\n91: ```\\n92: \\n93: ## Controlling time in tests\\n94: \\n95: In Envoy production code, time and timers are managed via\\n96: [`Event::TimeSystem`](https://github.com/envoyproxy/envoy/blob/main/include/envoy/event/timer.h),\\n97: which provides a mechanism for querying the time and setting up time-based\\n98: callbacks. Bypassing this abstraction in Envoy code is flagged as a format\\n99: violation in CI.\\n100: \\n101: In tests we use a derivation\\n102: [`Event::TestTimeSystem`](test_common/test_time_system.h) which adds the ability\\n103: to sleep or do a blocking timed wait on a condition variable. There are two\\n104: implementations of the `Event::TestTimeSystem` interface:\\n105: `Event::TestRealTimeSystem`, and `Event::SimulatedTimeSystem`. The latter is\\n106: recommended for all new tests, as it helps avoid flaky tests on slow machines,\\n107: and makes tests run faster.\\n108: \\n109: Typically we do not want to have both real-time and simulated-time in the same\\n110: test; that could lead to hard-to-reproduce results. Thus both implementations\\n111: have a mechanism to enforce that only one of them can be instantiated at once.\\n112: A runtime assertion occurs if an `Event::TestRealTimeSystem` and\\n113: `Event::SimulatedTimeSystem` are instantiated at the same time. Once the\\n114: time-system goes out of scope, usually at the end of a test method, the slate\\n115: is clean and a new test-method can use a different time system.\\n116: \\n117: There is also `Event::GlobalTimeSystem`, which can be instantiated in shared\\n118: test infrastructure that wants to be agnostic to which `TimeSystem` is used in a\\n119: test. When no `TimeSystem` is instantiated in a test, the `Event::GlobalTimeSystem`\\n120: will lazy-initialize itself into a concrete `TimeSystem`. Currently this is\\n121: `TestRealTimeSystem` but will be changed in the future to `SimulatedTimeSystem`.\\n122: \\n123: \\n124: ## Benchmark tests\\n125: \\n126: Envoy uses [Google Benchmark](https://github.com/google/benchmark/) for\\n127: microbenchmarks. There are custom bazel rules, `envoy_cc_benchmark_binary` and\\n128: `envoy_benchmark_test`, to execute them locally and in CI environments\\n129: respectively. `envoy_benchmark_test` rules call the benchmark binary from a\\n130: [script](https://github.com/envoyproxy/envoy/blob/main/bazel/test_for_benchmark_wrapper.sh)\\n131: which runs the benchmark with a minimal number of iterations and skipping\\n132: expensive benchmarks to quickly verify that the binary is able to run to\\n133: completion. In order to collect meaningful bechmarks, `bazel run -c opt` the\\n134: benchmark binary target on a quiescent machine.\\n135: \\n136: If you would like to detect when your benchmark test is running under the\\n137: wrapper, call\\n138: [`Envoy::benchmark::skipExpensiveBechmarks()`](https://github.com/envoyproxy/envoy/blob/main/test/benchmark/main.h).\\n139: \",\"url\":\"https://sourcegraph.sourcegraph.com/github.com/sg-evals/envoy--v1.32.1@b35dd17bea856e19fc4e65fb05e68170841d3726/-/blob/test/README.md\"}"}]},"parent_tool_use_id":null,"session_id":"7a51d5b9-63f8-4c27-86d4-c47033ff4464","uuid":"fd7a2283-969a-4daa-9044-e0a42916bef3","tool_use_result":{"content":"{\"content\":\"1: # Envoy tests\\n2: \\n3: Envoy uses the [Google Test framework](https://github.com/google/googletest) for\\n4: tests, including\\n5: [Google Mock](https://github.com/google/googletest/blob/master/googlemock/README.md) for\\n6: mocks and matchers. See the documentation on those pages for information on the\\n7: various classes, macros, and matchers that Envoy uses from those frameworks.\\n8: \\n9: ## Integration tests\\n10: \\n11: Envoy contains an integration testing framework, for testing\\n12: downstream-Envoy-upstream communication.\\n13: [See the framework's README for more information.](https://github.com/envoyproxy/envoy/blob/main/test/integration/README.md)\\n14: \\n15: ## Custom matchers\\n16: \\n17: Envoy includes some custom Google Mock matchers to make test expectation\\n18: statements simpler to write and easier to understand.\\n19: \\n20: ### HeaderValueOf\\n21: \\n22: Tests that a HeaderMap argument contains exactly one header with the given key,\\n23: whose value satisfies the given expectation. The expectation can be a matcher,\\n24: or a string that the value should equal.\\n25: \\n26: Examples:\\n27: \\n28: ```cpp\\n29: EXPECT_THAT(response->headers(), HeaderValueOf(Headers::get().Server, \\\"envoy\\\"));\\n30: ```\\n31: \\n32: ```cpp\\n33: using testing::HasSubstr;\\n34: EXPECT_THAT(request->headers(),\\n35:             HeaderValueOf(Headers::get().AcceptEncoding, HasSubstr(\\\"gzip\\\")));\\n36: ```\\n37: \\n38: ### HttpStatusIs\\n39: \\n40: Tests that a HeaderMap argument has the provided HTTP status code. The status\\n41: code can be passed in as a string or an integer.\\n42: \\n43: Example:\\n44: \\n45: ```cpp\\n46: EXPECT_THAT(response->headers(), HttpStatusIs(\\\"200\\\"));\\n47: ```\\n48: \\n49: ### HeaderMapEqual and HeaderMapEqualRef\\n50: \\n51: `HeaderMapEqualRef` tests that two `HeaderMap` arguments are equal.\\n52: `HeaderMapEqual` is the same, but it compares two pointers to `HeaderMap`s, and\\n53: the matcher's argument must be a `HeaderMapPtr`.\\n54: \\n55: Example:\\n56: \\n57: ```cpp\\n58: EXPECT_THAT(response->headers(), HeaderMapEqualRef(expected_headers));\\n59: ```\\n60: \\n61: ### ProtoEq, ProtoEqIgnoringField, RepeatedProtoEq\\n62: \\n63: Tests equality of protobufs, with a variant that ignores the value (including\\n64: presence) of a single named field. Another variant can be used to compare two\\n65: instances of Protobuf::RepeatedPtrField element-by-element.\\n66: \\n67: Example:\\n68: \\n69: ```cpp\\n70: envoy::service::discovery::v3::DeltaDiscoveryRequest expected_request;\\n71: // (not shown: set some fields of expected_request...)\\n72: EXPECT_CALL(async_stream_, sendMessage(ProtoEqIgnoringField(expected_request, \\\"response_nonce\\\"), false));\\n73: \\n74: response->mutable_resources()->Add();\\n75: response->mutable_resources()->Add();\\n76: response->mutable_resources()->Add();\\n77: // (not shown: do something to populate those empty added items...)\\n78: EXPECT_CALL(callbacks_, onConfigUpdate(RepeatedProtoEq(response->resources()), version));\\n79: ```\\n80: \\n81: ### IsSubsetOfHeaders and IsSupersetOfHeaders\\n82: \\n83: Tests that one `HeaderMap` argument contains every header in another\\n84: `HeaderMap`.\\n85: \\n86: Examples:\\n87: \\n88: ```cpp\\n89: EXPECT_THAT(response->headers(), IsSubsetOfHeaders(allowed_headers));\\n90: EXPECT_THAT(response->headers(), IsSupersetOfHeaders(required_headers));\\n91: ```\\n92: \\n93: ## Controlling time in tests\\n94: \\n95: In Envoy production code, time and timers are managed via\\n96: [`Event::TimeSystem`](https://github.com/envoyproxy/envoy/blob/main/include/envoy/event/timer.h),\\n97: which provides a mechanism for querying the time and setting up time-based\\n98: callbacks. Bypassing this abstraction in Envoy code is flagged as a format\\n99: violation in CI.\\n100: \\n101: In tests we use a derivation\\n102: [`Event::TestTimeSystem`](test_common/test_time_system.h) which adds the ability\\n103: to sleep or do a blocking timed wait on a condition variable. There are two\\n104: implementations of the `Event::TestTimeSystem` interface:\\n105: `Event::TestRealTimeSystem`, and `Event::SimulatedTimeSystem`. The latter is\\n106: recommended for all new tests, as it helps avoid flaky tests on slow machines,\\n107: and makes tests run faster.\\n108: \\n109: Typically we do not want to have both real-time and simulated-time in the same\\n110: test; that could lead to hard-to-reproduce results. Thus both implementations\\n111: have a mechanism to enforce that only one of them can be instantiated at once.\\n112: A runtime assertion occurs if an `Event::TestRealTimeSystem` and\\n113: `Event::SimulatedTimeSystem` are instantiated at the same time. Once the\\n114: time-system goes out of scope, usually at the end of a test method, the slate\\n115: is clean and a new test-method can use a different time system.\\n116: \\n117: There is also `Event::GlobalTimeSystem`, which can be instantiated in shared\\n118: test infrastructure that wants to be agnostic to which `TimeSystem` is used in a\\n119: test. When no `TimeSystem` is instantiated in a test, the `Event::GlobalTimeSystem`\\n120: will lazy-initialize itself into a concrete `TimeSystem`. Currently this is\\n121: `TestRealTimeSystem` but will be changed in the future to `SimulatedTimeSystem`.\\n122: \\n123: \\n124: ## Benchmark tests\\n125: \\n126: Envoy uses [Google Benchmark](https://github.com/google/benchmark/) for\\n127: microbenchmarks. There are custom bazel rules, `envoy_cc_benchmark_binary` and\\n128: `envoy_benchmark_test`, to execute them locally and in CI environments\\n129: respectively. `envoy_benchmark_test` rules call the benchmark binary from a\\n130: [script](https://github.com/envoyproxy/envoy/blob/main/bazel/test_for_benchmark_wrapper.sh)\\n131: which runs the benchmark with a minimal number of iterations and skipping\\n132: expensive benchmarks to quickly verify that the binary is able to run to\\n133: completion. In order to collect meaningful bechmarks, `bazel run -c opt` the\\n134: benchmark binary target on a quiescent machine.\\n135: \\n136: If you would like to detect when your benchmark test is running under the\\n137: wrapper, call\\n138: [`Envoy::benchmark::skipExpensiveBechmarks()`](https://github.com/envoyproxy/envoy/blob/main/test/benchmark/main.h).\\n139: \",\"url\":\"https://sourcegraph.sourcegraph.com/github.com/sg-evals/envoy--v1.32.1@b35dd17bea856e19fc4e65fb05e68170841d3726/-/blob/test/README.md\"}","structuredContent":{"content":"1: # Envoy tests\n2: \n3: Envoy uses the [Google Test framework](https://github.com/google/googletest) for\n4: tests, including\n5: [Google Mock](https://github.com/google/googletest/blob/master/googlemock/README.md) for\n6: mocks and matchers. See the documentation on those pages for information on the\n7: various classes, macros, and matchers that Envoy uses from those frameworks.\n8: \n9: ## Integration tests\n10: \n11: Envoy contains an integration testing framework, for testing\n12: downstream-Envoy-upstream communication.\n13: [See the framework's README for more information.](https://github.com/envoyproxy/envoy/blob/main/test/integration/README.md)\n14: \n15: ## Custom matchers\n16: \n17: Envoy includes some custom Google Mock matchers to make test expectation\n18: statements simpler to write and easier to understand.\n19: \n20: ### HeaderValueOf\n21: \n22: Tests that a HeaderMap argument contains exactly one header with the given key,\n23: whose value satisfies the given expectation. The expectation can be a matcher,\n24: or a string that the value should equal.\n25: \n26: Examples:\n27: \n28: ```cpp\n29: EXPECT_THAT(response->headers(), HeaderValueOf(Headers::get().Server, \"envoy\"));\n30: ```\n31: \n32: ```cpp\n33: using testing::HasSubstr;\n34: EXPECT_THAT(request->headers(),\n35:             HeaderValueOf(Headers::get().AcceptEncoding, HasSubstr(\"gzip\")));\n36: ```\n37: \n38: ### HttpStatusIs\n39: \n40: Tests that a HeaderMap argument has the provided HTTP status code. The status\n41: code can be passed in as a string or an integer.\n42: \n43: Example:\n44: \n45: ```cpp\n46: EXPECT_THAT(response->headers(), HttpStatusIs(\"200\"));\n47: ```\n48: \n49: ### HeaderMapEqual and HeaderMapEqualRef\n50: \n51: `HeaderMapEqualRef` tests that two `HeaderMap` arguments are equal.\n52: `HeaderMapEqual` is the same, but it compares two pointers to `HeaderMap`s, and\n53: the matcher's argument must be a `HeaderMapPtr`.\n54: \n55: Example:\n56: \n57: ```cpp\n58: EXPECT_THAT(response->headers(), HeaderMapEqualRef(expected_headers));\n59: ```\n60: \n61: ### ProtoEq, ProtoEqIgnoringField, RepeatedProtoEq\n62: \n63: Tests equality of protobufs, with a variant that ignores the value (including\n64: presence) of a single named field. Another variant can be used to compare two\n65: instances of Protobuf::RepeatedPtrField element-by-element.\n66: \n67: Example:\n68: \n69: ```cpp\n70: envoy::service::discovery::v3::DeltaDiscoveryRequest expected_request;\n71: // (not shown: set some fields of expected_request...)\n72: EXPECT_CALL(async_stream_, sendMessage(ProtoEqIgnoringField(expected_request, \"response_nonce\"), false));\n73: \n74: response->mutable_resources()->Add();\n75: response->mutable_resources()->Add();\n76: response->mutable_resources()->Add();\n77: // (not shown: do something to populate those empty added items...)\n78: EXPECT_CALL(callbacks_, onConfigUpdate(RepeatedProtoEq(response->resources()), version));\n79: ```\n80: \n81: ### IsSubsetOfHeaders and IsSupersetOfHeaders\n82: \n83: Tests that one `HeaderMap` argument contains every header in another\n84: `HeaderMap`.\n85: \n86: Examples:\n87: \n88: ```cpp\n89: EXPECT_THAT(response->headers(), IsSubsetOfHeaders(allowed_headers));\n90: EXPECT_THAT(response->headers(), IsSupersetOfHeaders(required_headers));\n91: ```\n92: \n93: ## Controlling time in tests\n94: \n95: In Envoy production code, time and timers are managed via\n96: [`Event::TimeSystem`](https://github.com/envoyproxy/envoy/blob/main/include/envoy/event/timer.h),\n97: which provides a mechanism for querying the time and setting up time-based\n98: callbacks. Bypassing this abstraction in Envoy code is flagged as a format\n99: violation in CI.\n100: \n101: In tests we use a derivation\n102: [`Event::TestTimeSystem`](test_common/test_time_system.h) which adds the ability\n103: to sleep or do a blocking timed wait on a condition variable. There are two\n104: implementations of the `Event::TestTimeSystem` interface:\n105: `Event::TestRealTimeSystem`, and `Event::SimulatedTimeSystem`. The latter is\n106: recommended for all new tests, as it helps avoid flaky tests on slow machines,\n107: and makes tests run faster.\n108: \n109: Typically we do not want to have both real-time and simulated-time in the same\n110: test; that could lead to hard-to-reproduce results. Thus both implementations\n111: have a mechanism to enforce that only one of them can be instantiated at once.\n112: A runtime assertion occurs if an `Event::TestRealTimeSystem` and\n113: `Event::SimulatedTimeSystem` are instantiated at the same time. Once the\n114: time-system goes out of scope, usually at the end of a test method, the slate\n115: is clean and a new test-method can use a different time system.\n116: \n117: There is also `Event::GlobalTimeSystem`, which can be instantiated in shared\n118: test infrastructure that wants to be agnostic to which `TimeSystem` is used in a\n119: test. Currently this is\n121: `TestRealTimeSystem` but will be changed in the future to `SimulatedTimeSystem`.\n122: \n123: \n124: ## Benchmark tests\n125: \n126: Envoy uses [Google Benchmark](https://github.com/google/benchmark/) for\n127: microbenchmarks. There are custom bazel rules, `envoy_cc_benchmark_binary` and\n128: `envoy_benchmark_test`, to execute them locally and in CI environments\n129: respectively. `envoy_benchmark_test` rules call the benchmark binary from a\n130: [script](https://github.com/envoyproxy/envoy/blob/main/bazel/test_for_benchmark_wrapper.sh)\n131: which runs the benchmark with a minimal number of iterations and skipping\n132: expensive benchmarks to quickly verify that the binary is able to run to\n133: completion. In order to collect meaningful bechmarks, `bazel run -c opt` the\n134: benchmark binary target on a quiescent machine.\n135: \n136: If you would like to detect when your benchmark test is running under the\n137: wrapper, call\n138: [`Envoy::benchmark::skipExpensiveBechmarks()`](https://github.com/envoyproxy/envoy/blob/main/test/benchmark/main.h).\n139: ","url":"https://sourcegraph.sourcegraph.com/github.com/sg-evals/envoy--v1.32.1@b35dd17bea856e19fc4e65fb05e68170841d3726/-/blob/test/README.md"}}}

{"type":"user","message":{"role":"user","content":[{"tool_use_id":"toolu_01KWQjD311A8ESMCMQPhYnHM","type":"tool_result","content":"{\"content\":\"1: # C++ coding style\\n2: \\n3: * The Envoy source code is formatted using clang-format. Thus all white spaces, etc.\\n4:   issues are taken care of automatically. The Azure Pipelines will automatically check\\n5:   the code format and fail. There are make targets that can both check the format\\n6:   (check_format) as well as fix the code format for you (fix_format). Errors in\\n7:   .clang-tidy are enforced while other warnings are suggestions. Note that code and\\n8:   comment blocks designated `clang-format off` must be closed with `clang-format on`.\\n9:   To run these checks locally, see [Support Tools](support/README.md).\\n10: * Beyond code formatting, for the most part Envoy uses the\\n11:   [Google C++ style guidelines](https://google.github.io/styleguide/cppguide.html).\\n12:   The following section covers the major areas where we deviate from the Google\\n13:   guidelines.\\n14: \\n15: # Repository file layout\\n16: \\n17: * Please see [REPO_LAYOUT.md](REPO_LAYOUT.md).\\n18: \\n19: # Documentation\\n20: \\n21: * If you are modifying the data plane structurally, please keep the [Life of a\\n22:   Request](https://www.envoyproxy.io/docs/envoy/latest/intro/life_of_a_request) documentation up-to-date.\\n23: \\n24: # Deviations from Google C++ style guidelines\\n25: \\n26: * Exceptions are allowed on the control plane, though now discouraged in new code. Adding exceptions is disallowed on the data plane.\\n27: * References are always preferred over pointers when the reference cannot be null. This\\n28:   includes both const and non-const references.\\n29: * Function names should all use camel case starting with a lower case letter (e.g., `doFoo()`).\\n30: * Struct/Class member variables have a `_` postfix (e.g., `int foo_;`).\\n31: * Enum values using PascalCase (e.g., `RoundRobin`).\\n32: * 100 columns is the line limit.\\n33: * Use your GitHub name in TODO comments, e.g. `TODO(foobar): blah`.\\n34: * Smart pointers are type aliased:\\n35:   * `using FooPtr = std::unique_ptr<Foo>;`\\n36:   * `using BarSharedPtr = std::shared_ptr<Bar>;`\\n37:   * `using BlahConstSharedPtr = std::shared_ptr<const Blah>;`\\n38:   * Regular pointers (e.g. `int* foo`) should not be type aliased.\\n39: * `absl::optional<std::reference_wrapper<T>>` has a helper class in `envoy/common/optref.h`, and is type aliased:\\n40:   * `using FooOptRef = OptRef<T>;`\\n41:   * `using FooOptConstRef = OptRef<const T>;`\\n42: * If move semantics are intended, prefer specifying function arguments with `&&`.\\n43:   E.g., `void onHeaders(Http::HeaderMapPtr&& headers, ...)`. The rationale for this is that it\\n44:   forces the caller to specify `std::move(...)` or pass a temporary and makes the intention at\\n45:   the callsite clear. Otherwise, it's difficult to tell if a const reference is actually being\\n46:   passed to the called function. This is true even for `std::unique_ptr`.\\n47: * Prefer `unique_ptr` over `shared_ptr` wherever possible. `unique_ptr` makes ownership in\\n48:   production code easier to reason about. Note that this creates some test oddities where\\n49:   production code requires a `unique_ptr` but the test must still have access to the memory\\n50:   the production code is using (mock or otherwise). In these cases it is acceptable to allocate\\n51:   raw memory in a test and return it to the production code with the expectation that the\\n52:   production code will hold it in a `unique_ptr` and free it. Envoy uses the factory pattern\\n53:   quite a bit for these cases. (Search the code for \\\"factory\\\").\\n54: * Prefer explicitly sized integer types, such as uint64_t rather than size_t. In particular, use\\n55:   explicitly sized integers for data that is written to disk or involved in math that might overflow.\\n56: * The Google C++ style guide points out that [non-PoD static and global variables are forbidden](https://google.github.io/styleguide/cppguide.html#Static_and_Global_Variables).\\n57:   This _includes_ types such as `std::string`. We encourage the use of the\\n58:   advice in the [C++ FAQ on the static initialization\\n59:   fiasco](https://isocpp.org/wiki/faq/ctors#static-init-order-on-first-use) for\\n60:   how to best handle this.\\n61: * The Google C++ style guide points out that [constant vars should be named `kConstantVar`](https://google.github.io/styleguide/cppguide.html#Constant_Names).\\n62:   In the Envoy codebase we use `ConstantVar` or `CONSTANT_VAR`. If you pick `CONSTANT_VAR`,\\n63:   please be certain the name is globally significant to avoid potential conflicts with #defines,\\n64:   which are not namespace-scoped, and may appear in externally controlled header files.\\n65: * API-level comments should follow normal Doxygen conventions. Use `@param` to describe\\n66:   parameters and `@return <return-type>` for return values. Internal comments for\\n67:   methods and member variables may be regular C++ `//` comments or Doxygen at\\n68:   developer discretion. Where possible, methods should have meaningful\\n69:   documentation on expected input and state preconditions.\\n70: * Header guards should use `#pragma once`.\\n71: * All code should be inside a top-level Envoy namespace. There are some\\n72:   exceptions such as `main()` functions. When code cannot be placed inside the\\n73:   Envoy namespace there should be a comment of the form `// NOLINT(namespace-envoy)` at\\n74:   the top of the file.\\n75: * If a method that must be defined outside the `test` directory is intended to be called only\\n76:   from test code then it should have a name that ends in `ForTest()` such as `aMethodForTest()`.\\n77:   In most cases tests can and should be structured so this is not necessary.\\n78: * Tests default to StrictMock so will fail if hitting unexpected warnings. Feel free to use\\n79:   NiceMock for mocks whose behavior is not the focus of a test.\\n80: * [Thread\\n81:   annotations](https://github.com/abseil/abseil-cpp/blob/master/absl/base/thread_annotations.h),\\n82:   such as `ABSL_GUARDED_BY`, should be used for shared state guarded by\\n83:   locks/mutexes.\\n84: * Functions intended to be local to a cc file should be declared in an anonymous namespace,\\n85:   rather than using the 'static' keyword. Note that the\\n86:   [Google C++ style guide](https://google.github.io/styleguide/cppguide.html#Unnamed_Namespaces_and_Static_Variables)\\n87:    allows either, but in Envoy we prefer anonymous namespaces.\\n88: * Braces are required for all control statements include single line if, while, etc. statements.\\n89: * Don't use [mangled Protobuf enum\\n90:   names](https://developers.google.com/protocol-buffers/docs/reference/cpp-generated#enum).\\n91: \\n92: # Error handling\\n93: \\n94: A few general notes on our error handling philosophy:\\n95: \\n96: * All error code returns should be checked.\\n97: * At a very high level, our philosophy is that errors should be handled gracefully when caused by:\\n98:   - Untrusted network traffic (from downstream, upstream, or extensions like filters)\\n99:   - Raised by the Envoy process environment and are *likely* to happen\\n100:   - Third party dependency return codes\\n101: \",\"url\":\"https://sourcegraph.sourcegraph.com/github.com/sg-evals/envoy--v1.32.1@b35dd17bea856e19fc4e65fb05e68170841d3726/-/blob/STYLE.md%3FL1-100\"}"}]},"parent_tool_use_id":null,"session_id":"7a51d5b9-63f8-4c27-86d4-c47033ff4464","uuid":"96d97ebf-2400-4454-94e4-a990dc063c62","tool_use_result":{"content":"{\"content\":\"1: # C++ coding style\\n2: \\n3: * The Envoy source code is formatted using clang-format. Thus all white spaces, etc.\\n4:   issues are taken care of automatically. The Azure Pipelines will automatically check\\n5:   the code format and fail. There are make targets that can both check the format\\n6:   (check_format) as well as fix the code format for you (fix_format). Errors in\\n7:   .clang-tidy are enforced while other warnings are suggestions. Note that code and\\n8:   comment blocks designated `clang-format off` must be closed with `clang-format on`.\\n9:   To run these checks locally, see [Support Tools](support/README.md).\\n10: * Beyond code formatting, for the most part Envoy uses the\\n11:   [Google C++ style guidelines](https://google.github.io/styleguide/cppguide.html).\\n12:   The following section covers the major areas where we deviate from the Google\\n13:   guidelines.\\n14: \\n15: # Repository file layout\\n16: \\n17: * Please see [REPO_LAYOUT.md](REPO_LAYOUT.md).\\n18: \\n19: # Documentation\\n20: \\n21: * If you are modifying the data plane structurally, please keep the [Life of a\\n22:   Request](https://www.envoyproxy.io/docs/envoy/latest/intro/life_of_a_request) documentation up-to-date.\\n23: \\n24: # Deviations from Google C++ style guidelines\\n25: \\n26: * Exceptions are allowed on the control plane, though now discouraged in new code. Adding exceptions is disallowed on the data plane.\\n27: * References are always preferred over pointers when the reference cannot be null. This\\n28:   includes both const and non-const references.\\n29: * Function names should all use camel case starting with a lower case letter (e.g., `doFoo()`).\\n30: * Struct/Class member variables have a `_` postfix (e.g., `int foo_;`).\\n31: * Enum values using PascalCase (e.g., `RoundRobin`).\\n32: * 100 columns is the line limit.\\n33: * Use your GitHub name in TODO comments, e.g. `TODO(foobar): blah`.\\n34: * Smart pointers are type aliased:\\n35:   * `using FooPtr = std::unique_ptr<Foo>;`\\n36:   * `using BarSharedPtr = std::shared_ptr<Bar>;`\\n37:   * `using BlahConstSharedPtr = std::shared_ptr<const Blah>;`\\n38:   * Regular pointers (e.g. `int* foo`) should not be type aliased.\\n39: * `absl::optional<std::reference_wrapper<T>>` has a helper class in `envoy/common/optref.h`, and is type aliased:\\n40:   * `using FooOptRef = OptRef<T>;`\\n41:   * `using FooOptConstRef = OptRef<const T>;`\\n42: * If move semantics are intended, prefer specifying function arguments with `&&`.\\n43:   E.g., `void onHeaders(Http::HeaderMapPtr&& headers, ...)`. If you pick `CONSTANT_VAR`,\\n63:   please be certain the name is globally significant to avoid potential conflicts with #defines,\\n64:   which are not namespace-scoped, and may appear in externally controlled header files.\\n65: * API-level comments should follow normal Doxygen conventions. In the common case, one\\n5: \\n6: - Sends a request from downstream through Envoy\\n7: - Verifies the request is received upstream, and possibly inspects elements of the headers or body\\n8: - Sends a response from upstream through Envoy\\n9: - Verifies the request is received downstream, again possibly inspecting headers and body\\n10: \\n11: For the simplest variant of this, one could do the following.\\n12: \\n13: ```c++\\n14: // start Envoy, set up the fake upstreams.\\n15: initialize();\\n16: \\n17: // Create a client aimed at Envoy’s default HTTP port.\\n18: codec_client_ = makeHttpConnection(makeClientConnection((lookupPort(\\\"http\\\"))));\\n19: \\n20: // Create some request headers.\\n21: Http::TestRequestHeaderMapImpl request_headers{{\\\":method\\\", \\\"GET\\\"},\\n22:                                                {\\\":path\\\", \\\"/test/long/url\\\"},\\n23:                                                {\\\":scheme\\\", \\\"http\\\"},\\n24:                                                {\\\":authority\\\", \\\"host\\\"}};\\n25: \\n26: // Send the request headers from the client, wait until they are received upstream. There are existing tests which send requests with bodies, have\\n42: downstream or upstream disconnect or time out, send multiple simultaneous requests on the same\\n43: connection, etc. Given that many of the disconnect/timeout cases are covered, a common case for\\n44: testing is covering a newly added configuration option.\\n45: \\n46: Most of Envoy's tests have been migrated from using [`json flatfiles`](../config/integration/) to\\n47: using a basic configuration defined as `basic_config` in [`config/utility.cc`](../config/utility.cc).\\n48: This configuration may be modified before the call to `initialize()`.\\n49: The [`ConfigHelper`](../config/utility.h) has utilities for common alterations such as:\\n50: \\n51: ```c++\\n52: // Set the default protocol to HTTP2\\n53: setDownstreamProtocol(Http::CodecType::HTTP2);\\n54: ```\\n55: \\n56: or\\n57: \\n58: ```c++\\n59: // Add a buffering filter on the request path\\n60: config_helper_.prependFilter(ConfigHelper::DEFAULT_BUFFER_FILTER);\\n61: ```\\n62: \\n63: For other edits which are less likely reusable, one can add config modifiers. Build Prerequisites\n\n### Required Tools and Dependencies\n\nBefore building Envoy, you must install the following:\n\n**Bazel Build System:**\n- **Bazel version:** 6.5.0 (specified in `.bazelversion`)\n- **Installation:** Use [Bazelisk](https://github.com/bazelbuild/bazelisk) to automatically manage Bazel versions\n\n  Linux (x86_64/ARM64):\n  ```bash\n  sudo wget -O /usr/local/bin/bazel https://github.com/bazelbuild/bazelisk/releases/latest/download/bazelisk-linux-$([ $(uname -m) = \"aarch64\" ] && echo \"arm64\" || echo \"amd64\")\n  sudo chmod +x /usr/local/bin/bazel\n  ```\n\n  macOS:\n  ```bash\n  brew install bazelisk\n  ```\n\n**C++ Compiler Toolchain:**\n- **Ubuntu (primary CI environment):** GCC 9, Clang 14, based on Ubuntu 20.04 (Focal)\n- **CI Image:** `envoyproxy/envoy-build-ubuntu` with hash specified in `ci/envoy_build_sha.sh`\n\n**C++ Standard Library:**\n- Official releases use **libc++** on Linux (as of v1.21.0)\n- Override via environment: `export ENVOY_STDLIB=libc++` or `export ENVOY_STDLIB=libstdc++`\n\n**System Dependencies:**\n- Documented in [Envoy's official build documentation](https://www.envoyproxy.io/docs/envoy/latest/start/building#requirements)\n- In production, install independently; for development, use Docker containers\n\n**Development Support Toolchain (Recommended):**\n- Install via: `./support/bootstrap` (from repo root)\n- Provides Git hooks for:\n  - Automatic DCO sign-off generation\n  - Pre-push format validation\n  - Documentation: `support/README.md`\n\n## 2. Build System\n\n### Build System: Bazel\n\nEnvoy uses **Bazel** as its primary build system. All code is organized as Bazel targets with explicit dependencies.\n\n### Key Build Commands\n\n**Quick Start (Developer Build with Tests):**\n```bash\n# Using Docker (recommended for consistent environment)\n./ci/run_envoy_docker.sh './ci/do_ci.sh dev'\n```\n\n**Native Build (with dependencies installed):**\n```bash\n# Optimized build\nbazel build -c opt envoy\n\n# Debug build\nbazel build -c dbg envoy\n\n# Fastbuild (development, fastest)\nbazel build -c fastbuild envoy\n```\n\n**Build Specific Components:**\n```bash\n# Build a specific test\nbazel test //path/to:test_target\n\n# Build a specific library\nbazel build //path/to:library_target\n\n# Build with all contrib extensions\n./ci/run_envoy_docker.sh './ci/do_ci.sh dev.contrib'\n```\n\n### Build Configurations\n\n**Production/Release:**\n```bash\n./ci/run_envoy_docker.sh './ci/do_ci.sh release.server_only'\n# Output: `/tmp/envoy-docker-build/envoy/source/exe/envoy` (or custom `$ENVOY_DOCKER_BUILD_DIR`)\n```\n\n**Debug Build:**\n```bash\n./ci/run_envoy_docker.sh './ci/do_ci.sh debug.server_only'\n# Output: `/tmp/envoy-docker-build/envoy/source/exe/envoy-debug`\n```\n\n**Size-Optimized:**\n```bash\n./ci/run_envoy_docker.sh './ci/do_ci.sh sizeopt.server_only'\n```\n\n### Docker-Based Development\n\nThe recommended approach for consistent builds is using Docker:\n\n```bash\n# Basic invocation\n./ci/run_envoy_docker.sh './ci/do_ci.sh <target>'\n\n# Custom build directory\nENVOY_DOCKER_BUILD_DIR=~/build ./ci/run_envoy_docker.sh './ci/do_ci.sh dev'\n\n# Force Docker image refresh\nENVOY_DOCKER_PULL=true ./ci/run_envoy_docker.sh './ci/do_ci.sh dev'\n\n# Interactive Docker session\n./ci/run_envoy_docker.sh 'bash'\n```\n\n**Available Docker Images:**\n- `envoyproxy/envoy-build-ubuntu` (default, Ubuntu 20.04)\n- `envoyproxy/envoy-build-centos` (experimental)\n- Set via: `IMAGE_NAME=envoyproxy/envoy-build-ubuntu ./ci/run_envoy_docker.sh ...`\n\n### Build Configuration Files\n\n- `WORKSPACE`: Bazel workspace definition\n- `.bazelrc`: Bazel configuration (format, test options, etc.)\n- `bazel/`: Bazel rules and configurations\n- `BUILD`: Top-level Bazel build file\n\n## 3. Running Tests\n\n### Test Frameworks\n\nEnvoy uses:\n- **Unit Tests:** [Google Test (GTest)](https://github.com/google/googletest) + [Google Mock](https://github.com/google/googletest/blob/master/googlemock/README.md)\n- **Integration Tests:** Custom framework for testing downstream-Envoy-upstream communication\n- **Fuzz Tests:** libFuzzer-based tests with ASAN instrumentation\n- **Benchmark Tests:** Google Benchmark for microbenchmarks\n\n### Running Tests via Docker (Recommended)\n\n**All tests:**\n```bash\n./ci/run_envoy_docker.sh './ci/do_ci.sh dev'\n```\n\n**Specific test:**\n```bash\n./ci/run_envoy_docker.sh './ci/do_ci.sh dev //test/common/http:http_test'\n```\n\n**Test coverage report:**\n```bash\n./ci/run_envoy_docker.sh './ci/do_ci.sh coverage'\n# Output: `$ENVOY_DOCKER_BUILD_DIR/envoy/generated/coverage/coverage.html`\n```\n\n### Running Tests Natively (With Dependencies)\n\n```bash\n# Run all tests\nbazel test //...\n\n# Run specific test\nbazel test //test/common/http:http_test\n\n# Run test with debug symbols\nbazel test -c dbg //test/common/http:http_test\n\n# Run test matching pattern\nbazel test --test_tag_filters=tag //...\n```\n\n### Specialized Test Targets (via Docker)\n\n- `asan` — AddressSanitizer (memory errors)\n- `msan` — MemorySanitizer (uninitialized memory)\n- `tsan` — ThreadSanitizer (race conditions)\n- `fuzz` — libFuzzer-based fuzz tests\n- `compile_time_options` — Test with non-default compile flags\n- `coverage` — Generate coverage reports\n\nExample:\n```bash\n./ci/run_envoy_docker.sh './ci/do_ci.sh asan'\n./ci/run_envoy_docker.sh './ci/do_ci.sh tsan //test/common/http:http_test'\n```\n\n### Test Utilities and Helpers\n\n**Location:** `test/` directory mirrors `source/` structure\n- Unit tests: `test/common/`, `test/server/`, `test/exe/`\n- Integration tests: `test/integration/` with framework in `test/integration/integration.h`\n- Mocks: `test/mocks/` (mock implementations of core interfaces)\n- Test infrastructure: `test/test_common/` (time system, utilities)\n\n**Integration Test Framework:**\n- See: `test/integration/README.md`\n- Key helper: `ConfigHelper` (in `test/config/utility.h`) for modifying test configs\n- Autonomous upstream mode for simplified testing: set `autonomous_upstream_ = true`\n\n**Custom GTest Matchers:**\n- `HeaderValueOf()` — Check specific header values\n- `HttpStatusIs()` — Check HTTP status codes\n- `HeaderMapEqual()` / `HeaderMapEqualRef()` — Compare headers\n- `ProtoEq()` / `ProtoEqIgnoringField()` — Compare protobufs\n\n## 4. CI Pipeline\n\n### CI Platform\n\n**Primary:** [Azure Pipelines](https://dev.azure.com/cncf/envoy/_build)\n- Organization: `cncf`\n- Definition ID: 11\n- **Status badge:** [![Azure Pipelines](https://dev.azure.com/cncf/envoy/_apis/build/status/11?branchName=main)](https://dev.azure.com/cncf/envoy/_build/latest?definitionId=11&branchName=main)\n\n**Additional CI Systems:**\n- **Jenkins:** ppc64le builds (OSUOSL), s390x builds (OSUOSL)\n- **OSS-Fuzz:** Continuous fuzzing (Google)\n- **Zuul:** Additional platform-specific builds (referenced in `.zuul/`, `.zuul.yaml`)\n\n### CI Configuration Files\n\n- `.azure-pipelines/` — Azure Pipelines YAML configs\n- `ci/do_ci.sh` — Master build script (invoked by CI)\n- `ci/run_envoy_docker.sh` — Docker execution wrapper\n- `ci/mac_ci_setup.sh` / `ci/mac_ci_steps.sh` — macOS build\n- `ci/windows_ci_steps.sh` — Windows build (legacy, official support ended Aug 2023)\n- `ci/envoy_build_sha.sh` — Docker image hashes\n- `repokitteh.star` — Automation rules (GitHub checks, retesting)\n\n### CI Checks on Pull Requests\n\n**Standard checks:**\n1. **Build** — All supported platforms (Linux/Ubuntu, CentOS, macOS; ~~Windows~~)\n2. **Unit tests** — Google Test suite with multiple sanitizers (ASAN, MSAN, TSAN)\n3. **Integration tests** — End-to-end Envoy networking tests\n4. **Code coverage** — 100% coverage required for new code\n5. **Code formatting** — clang-format validation\n6. **Linting** — clang-tidy checks (error-level)\n7. **API/Proto checks** — Proto format and API versioning\n8. **Documentation** — Build and render docs\n\n**Typical CI run duration:** 1-2 hours (varies by change scope)\n\n### Triggering CI Retests\n\n**Rerun failed Azure Pipelines checks:**\n```\n/retest\n```\n(Comment on PR)\n\n**Force full CI re-run:**\n```bash\ngit commit -s --allow-empty -m 'Kick CI'\ngit push\n```\n\nOr use git alias:\n```bash\ngit config --add alias.kick-ci \"!git commit -s --allow-empty -m 'Kick CI' && git push\"\ngit kick-ci\n```\n\n### Remote Cache (Optional)\n\nAccelerate builds via Bazel remote cache:\n\n```bash\n# In .bazelrc or user.bazelrc:\nbuild:my-remote-cache --remote_cache=grpcs://remotecache.googleapis.com\nbuild:my-remote-cache --remote_cache_header=Authorization=\"Bearer <token>\"\n\n# Use in build:\nexport BAZEL_BUILD_EXTRA_OPTIONS=--config=my-remote-cache\n./ci/run_envoy_docker.sh './ci/do_ci.sh dev'\n```\n\n## 5. Code Review Process\n\n### Communication Before Starting Major Work\n\n**Required for significant changes (>100 LOC, user-facing behavior):**\n1. **Open a GitHub issue** to discuss the feature/bug\n2. **Get maintainer agreement** before coding\n3. **Prevents:** wasted effort, design disagreements, duplicate work\n\n**Not required for:** Small bug fixes, docs changes\n\n**For new extensions:** See `EXTENSION_POLICY.md` for policy and requirements\n\n**Relevant mailing lists:**\n- `envoy-dev@googlegroups.com` — Discussions, design proposals\n- `envoy-announce@googlegroups.com` — Announcements (for deprecations/breaking changes)\n- `envoy-security@googlegroups.com` — Security vulnerabilities\n\n### Submitting a Pull Request\n\n**Setup:**\n```bash\n# Fork repo on GitHub\n# Clone and install git hooks\ngit clone https://github.com/YOUR_USERNAME/envoy.git\ncd envoy\n./support/bootstrap  # Installs git hooks for DCO + format checks\n```\n\n**Create PR:**\n1. **Branch off `main`:** `git checkout -b your-feature-branch`\n2. **Write code** with tests (100% coverage for new code)\n3. **Commit with DCO sign-off:**\n   ```bash\n   git commit -s -m \"component: description\"\n   # or auto-added by support/bootstrap hook\n   ```\n4. **Push to your fork** and open PR on GitHub\n\n### PR Title and Message Format\n\n**Title format:** `component: description` (lowercase)\n\nExamples:\n- `docs: fix grammar error`\n- `http conn man: add new feature`\n- `router: add x-envoy-overloaded header`\n- `tls: add support for TLS session ticket keys`\n\n**Commit message:**\n- Explain what changed and why\n- If fixing issue: `Fixes #XXX`\n- For behavioral changes: document before/after behavior\n- For deprecations: list what's deprecated\n\n**Use pull request template:** Automatically filled in when you open a PR\n- **Risk level:** Low | Medium | High\n- **Testing:** Describe testing performed\n- **Documentation:** Link to docs/release notes changes\n- **Release notes:** Update `changelogs/current.yaml` for user-facing changes\n- **API changes:** Reference [API Review Checklist](api/review_checklist.md)\n\n### DCO Sign-Off\n\nAll commits must be signed off with Developer Certificate of Origin:\n\n```bash\ngit commit -s  # Adds: Signed-off-by: Your Name <your.email@example.com>\n```\n\nAuto-signup via git alias:\n```bash\ngit config --add alias.c \"commit -s\"\n```\n\n**Fix DCO errors on existing PR:**\n```bash\ngit rebase -i HEAD~N  # Squash commits\ngit commit -s --amend  # Add sign-off\ngit push origin -f  # Force push (acceptable only for DCO fixes)\n```\n\n### PR Review Requirements\n\n- **Tests must pass** — No PRs merge with failing tests\n- **100% code coverage** — All new code must be covered by tests (or justified)\n- **Cross-company reviews** — For new extensions: at least one approver from a different organization than the author\n- **Senior maintainer review** — Core code requires senior maintainer approval\n- **Domain expert review** — Code should be reviewed by area expert (not necessarily maintainer)\n\n**Maintainers and reviewers:** See `OWNERS.md` for area experts\n\n### Coding Standards\n\n**Format:** Automatically enforced via clang-format\n- Line limit: 100 characters\n- Run fixes: `bazel run //tools/code_format:check_format -- fix`\n\n**Style:** [Google C++ style guide](https://google.github.io/styleguide/cppguide.html) with Envoy deviations:\n- Function names: camelCase starting lowercase (e.g., `doFoo()`)\n- Member variables: trailing underscore (e.g., `foo_`)\n- Enum values: PascalCase (e.g., `RoundRobin`)\n- Smart pointers: type aliased (e.g., `using FooPtr = std::unique_ptr<Foo>;`)\n- `#pragma once` for header guards\n- Code inside `Envoy` namespace\n- Anonymous namespaces preferred over `static`\n- Inclusive language policy: no \"whitelist\"/\"blacklist\"/\"master\"/\"slave\" terms\n\n**Linting:** clang-tidy (error-level enforced)\n\n**Inclusive language:**\n- ❌ \"whitelist\" → ✅ \"allowlist\"\n- ❌ \"blacklist\" → ✅ \"denylist\"/\"blocklist\"\n- ❌ \"master\" → ✅ \"primary\"/\"main\"\n- ❌ \"slave\" → ✅ \"secondary\"/\"replica\"\n\n### Important PR Guidelines\n\n- **Don't rebase after review starts** — GitHub forces reviewers to re-review everything\n- Use merge to pull main changes:\n  ```bash\n  git checkout main && git pull && git checkout your-branch && git merge main\n  ```\n- **Format checks:** Run pre-push checks locally via `./support/bootstrap`\n- **Don't use `--no-verify`** for hooks unless absolutely necessary (bypasses critical checks)\n- **Stale PRs:** PRs with >7 days of inactivity may be closed; can be reopened\n- **Pro-actively work on PR** — Don't abandon after opening\n- **Don't force push** after review starts (exception: DCO sign-off fixes)\n\n### PR Review Timeline\n\n- **Expected response:** Within one business day\n- **Senior maintainer:** Reviews all core code changes\n- **Domain experts:** Should review relevant areas (may not be maintainers)\n- **Anyone can review:** Community reviews welcome\n\n### Merging\n\n**Before merge:**\n1. All tests pass\n2. Coverage ≥100% for new code\n3. All documentation updated\n4. Release notes added (if user-facing)\n5. PR title/body cleaned up by maintainer\n\n**After merge:**\n- If PR has deprecations: notification sent to `envoy-announce@`\n- Squash merge used (commit history cleaned)\n- Maintainer ensures final commit message is correct\n\n### Runtime Guarding (High-Risk Changes)\n\nSome changes (major refactors, behavioral changes to HTTP processing) require runtime guards:\n\n```cpp\nif (Runtime::runtimeFeatureEnabled(\"envoy.reloadable_features.my_feature_name\")) {\n  [new code path]\n} else {\n  [old_code_path]\n}\n```\n\n- Both paths must have 100% coverage\n- May be enabled by default or after testing period\n- See: `source/common/runtime/runtime_features.cc`\n- Reference: `CONTRIBUTING.md` \"Runtime Guarding\" section\n\n## 6. Developer Workflow Example\n\n### Scenario: Fix bug in HTTP Connection Manager filter\n\n**Step 1: Discuss with community**\n```\n1. Search existing issues: Is this already tracked?\n2. If not, open GitHub issue: \"HTTP Connection Manager: [description of bug]\"\n3. Wait for confirmation from maintainers that it's not in progress\n```\n\n**Step 2: Set up development environment**\n```bash\n# Clone and setup\ngit clone https://github.com/YOUR_USERNAME/envoy.git\ncd envoy\n./support/bootstrap\n\n# Create feature branch\ngit checkout -b fix/http-conn-man-bug\n```\n\n**Step 3: Understand the codebase**\n```bash\n# HTTP Connection Manager code locations:\n# - Core: source/common/http/conn_manager_impl.cc/h\n# - Tests: test/common/http/conn_manager_impl_test.cc\n# - Integration: test/integration/ (various HTTP tests)\n\n# Search for references:\ngrep -r \"conn_manager_impl\" source/\n```\n\n**Step 4: Write tests first**\n```bash\n# Add failing test to test/common/http/conn_manager_impl_test.cc\n# Build and verify it fails\n./ci/run_envoy_docker.sh './ci/do_ci.sh dev //test/common/http:conn_manager_impl_test'\n```\n\n**Step 5: Implement the fix**\n```bash\n# Edit source/common/http/conn_manager_impl.cc\n# Follow style guide and coding standards\n```\n\n**Step 6: Run full test suite locally**\n```bash\n# Run all HTTP-related tests\n./ci/run_envoy_docker.sh './ci/do_ci.sh dev //test/common/http/...'\n\n# Run with sanitizers\n./ci/run_envoy_docker.sh './ci/do_ci.sh asan'\n\n# Check code formatting\nbazel run //tools/code_format:check_format -- fix\n```\n\n**Step 7: Commit and push**\n```bash\n# Commit with DCO sign-off\ngit add source/common/http/conn_manager_impl.{cc,h} test/common/http/conn_manager_impl_test.cc\ngit commit -s -m \"http conn man: fix [specific issue]\n\nFixes #ISSUE_NUMBER\n\nThis commit fixes the HTTP connection manager by [explanation of fix].\nThe bug occurred when [reproduction steps]. This is now fixed by\n[explanation of solution].\"\n\n# Push to fork\ngit push origin fix/http-conn-man-bug\n```\n\n**Step 8: Open PR on GitHub**\n```\n1. Go to: https://github.com/envoyproxy/envoy/compare/main...YOUR_USERNAME:fix/http-conn-man-bug\n2. Fill in PR template:\n   - Title: \"http conn man: fix [issue]\"\n   - Risk: Low (if small fix) | Medium (if moderate) | High (if major)\n   - Testing: \"Added unit test in test/common/http/conn_manager_impl_test.cc\"\n   - Documentation: \"N/A\" or link to docs changes\n   - Release notes: Add entry to changelogs/current.yaml\n   - Issues: \"Fixes #ISSUE_NUMBER\"\n3. Submit PR\n```\n\n**Step 9: Wait for CI and review**\n```\n1. Azure Pipelines runs (1-2 hours):\n   - Builds on Linux (Ubuntu, CentOS)\n   - macOS build\n   - All tests run\n   - Coverage checked\n   - Code formatting verified\n2. Maintainers and domain experts review\n3. Address feedback (new commits, don't rebase)\n```\n\n**Step 10: Merge**\n```\n1. All tests pass ✓\n2. All reviews approved ✓\n3. Maintainer merges with squash\n4. Your fix is in main!\n5. Celebrate! 🎉\n```\n\n### Key Commands Cheat Sheet\n\n```bash\n# Setup\ngit clone https://github.com/YOUR_USERNAME/envoy.git && cd envoy\n./support/bootstrap\n\n# Development\ngit checkout -b feature-name\n\n# Build and test (Docker)\n./ci/run_envoy_docker.sh './ci/do_ci.sh dev'\n./ci/run_envoy_docker.sh './ci/do_ci.sh dev //test/specific:test_target'\n./ci/run_envoy_docker.sh './ci/do_ci.sh asan'  # AddressSanitizer\n./ci/run_envoy_docker.sh './ci/do_ci.sh coverage'\n\n# Format\nbazel run //tools/code_format:check_format -- fix\n\n# Commit\ngit add [files]\ngit commit -s -m \"component: description\"\n\n# Push\ngit push origin feature-name\n\n# Rebase incoming changes (don't force push)\ngit checkout main && git pull\ngit checkout feature-name && git merge main\n\n# Rerun CI\n# (comment on PR): /retest\n# Or: git commit -s --allow-empty -m 'Kick CI' && git push\n```\n\n---\n\n## Additional Resources\n\n- **Build:** `bazel/README.md`\n- **Tests:** `test/README.md`, `test/integration/README.md`\n- **External dependencies:** `bazel/EXTERNAL_DEPS.md`\n- **Bazel rules guide:** `bazel/DEVELOPER.md`\n- **Extension policy:** `EXTENSION_POLICY.md`\n- **API versioning:** `api/API_VERSIONING.md`\n- **API review checklist:** `api/review_checklist.md`\n- **Repository layout:** `REPO_LAYOUT.md`\n- **Development toolchain:** `support/README.md`\n- **VS Code setup:** `tools/vscode/README.md`\n\n## Community\n\n- **Slack:** https://envoyproxy.slack.com/ (for quick questions)\n- **Mailing lists:** envoy-dev@, envoy-users@, envoy-announce@ (for announcements)\n- **Community meeting:** Bi-weekly on Tuesdays at 9am PT (see public [calendar](https://goo.gl/PkDijT))\n- **Code of conduct:** `CODE_OF_CONDUCT.md`\n"},"caller":{"type":"direct"}}],"stop_reason":null,"stop_sequence":null,"usage":{"input_tokens":12,"cache_creation_input_tokens":6308,"cache_read_input_tokens":65559,"cache_creation":{"ephemeral_5m_input_tokens":0,"ephemeral_1h_input_tokens":6308},"output_tokens":3,"service_tier":"standard","inference_geo":"not_available"},"context_management":null},"parent_tool_use_id":null,"session_id":"7a51d5b9-63f8-4c27-86d4-c47033ff4464","uuid":"2e36e70f-91e7-4f46-bc2c-23768b55acca"}

Dependencies)\n\n```bash\n# Run all tests\nbazel test //...\n\n# Run specific test\nbazel test //test/common/http:http_test\n\n# Run test with debug symbols\nbazel test -c dbg //test/common/http:http_test\n\n# Run test matching pattern\nbazel test --test_tag_filters=tag //...\n```\n\n### Specialized Test Targets (via Docker)\n\n- `asan` — AddressSanitizer (memory errors)\n- `msan` — MemorySanitizer (uninitialized memory)\n- `tsan` — ThreadSanitizer (race conditions)\n- `fuzz` — libFuzzer-based fuzz tests\n- `compile_time_options` — Test with non-default compile flags\n- `coverage` — Generate coverage reports\n\nExample:\n```bash\n./ci/run_envoy_docker.sh './ci/do_ci.sh asan'\n./ci/run_envoy_docker.sh './ci/do_ci.sh tsan //test/common/http:http_test'\n```\n\n### Test Utilities and Helpers\n\n**Location:** `test/` directory mirrors `source/` structure\n- Unit tests: `test/common/`, `test/server/`, `test/exe/`\n- Integration tests: `test/integration/` with framework in `test/integration/integration.h`\n- Mocks: `test/mocks/` (mock implementations of core interfaces)\n- Test infrastructure: `test/test_common/` (time system, utilities)\n\n**Integration Test Framework:**\n- See: `test/integration/README.md`\n- Key helper: `ConfigHelper` (in `test/config/utility.h`) for modifying test configs\n- Autonomous upstream mode for simplified testing: set `autonomous_upstream_ = true`\n\n**Custom GTest Matchers:**\n- `HeaderValueOf()` — Check specific header values\n- `HttpStatusIs()` — Check HTTP status codes\n- `HeaderMapEqual()` / `HeaderMapEqualRef()` — Compare headers\n- `ProtoEq()` / `ProtoEqIgnoringField()` — Compare protobufs\n\n## 4. CI Pipeline\n\n### CI Platform\n\n**Primary:** [Azure Pipelines](https://dev.azure.com/cncf/envoy/_build)\n- Organization: `cncf`\n- Definition ID: 11\n- **Status badge:** [![Azure Pipelines](https://dev.azure.com/cncf/envoy/_apis/build/status/11?branchName=main)](https://dev.azure.com/cncf/envoy/_build/latest?definitionId=11&branchName=main)\n\n**Additional CI Systems:**\n- **Jenkins:** ppc64le builds (OSUOSL), s390x builds (OSUOSL)\n- **OSS-Fuzz:** Continuous fuzzing (Google)\n- **Zuul:** Additional platform-specific builds (referenced in `.zuul/`, `.zuul.yaml`)\n\n### CI Configuration Files\n\n- `.azure-pipelines/` — Azure Pipelines YAML configs\n- `ci/do_ci.sh` — Master build script (invoked by CI)\n- `ci/run_envoy_docker.sh` — Docker execution wrapper\n- `ci/mac_ci_setup.sh` / `ci/mac_ci_steps.sh` — macOS build\n- `ci/windows_ci_steps.sh` — Windows build (legacy, official support ended Aug 2023)\n- `ci/envoy_build_sha.sh` — Docker image hashes\n- `repokitteh.star` — Automation rules (GitHub checks, retesting)\n\n### CI Checks on Pull Requests\n\n**Standard checks:**\n1. **Build** — All supported platforms (Linux/Ubuntu, CentOS, macOS; ~~Windows~~)\n2. **Unit tests** — Google Test suite with multiple sanitizers (ASAN, MSAN, TSAN)\n3. **Integration tests** — End-to-end Envoy networking tests\n4. **Code coverage** — 100% coverage required for new code\n5. **Code formatting** — clang-format validation\n6. **Linting** — clang-tidy checks (error-level)\n7. **API/Proto checks** — Proto format and API versioning\n8. **Documentation** — Build and render docs\n\n**Typical CI run duration:** 1-2 hours (varies by change scope)\n\n### Triggering CI Retests\n\n**Rerun failed Azure Pipelines checks:**\n```\n/retest\n```\n(Comment on PR)\n\n**Force full CI re-run:**\n```bash\ngit commit -s --allow-empty -m 'Kick CI'\ngit push\n```\n\nOr use git alias:\n```bash\ngit config --add alias.kick-ci \"!git commit -s --allow-empty -m 'Kick CI' && git push\"\ngit kick-ci\n```\n\n### Remote Cache (Optional)\n\nAccelerate builds via Bazel remote cache:\n\n```bash\n# In .bazelrc or user.bazelrc:\nbuild:my-remote-cache --remote_cache=grpcs://remotecache.googleapis.com\nbuild:my-remote-cache --remote_cache_header=Authorization=\"Bearer <token>\"\n\n# Use in build:\nexport BAZEL_BUILD_EXTRA_OPTIONS=--config=my-remote-cache\n./ci/run_envoy_docker.sh './ci/do_ci.sh dev'\n```\n\n## 5. Code Review Process\n\n### Communication Before Starting Major Work\n\n**Required for significant changes (>100 LOC, user-facing behavior):**\n1. **Open a GitHub issue** to discuss the feature/bug\n2. **Get maintainer agreement** before coding\n3. **Prevents:** wasted effort, design disagreements, duplicate work\n\n**Not required for:** Small bug fixes, docs changes\n\n**For new extensions:** See `EXTENSION_POLICY.md` for policy and requirements\n\n**Relevant mailing lists:**\n- `envoy-dev@googlegroups.com` — Discussions, design proposals\n- `envoy-announce@googlegroups.com` — Announcements (for deprecations/breaking changes)\n- `envoy-security@googlegroups.com` — Security vulnerabilities\n\n### Submitting a Pull Request\n\n**Setup:**\n```bash\n# Fork repo on GitHub\n# Clone and install git hooks\ngit clone https://github.com/YOUR_USERNAME/envoy.git\ncd envoy\n./support/bootstrap  # Installs git hooks for DCO + format checks\n```\n\n**Create PR:**\n1. **Branch off `main`:** `git checkout -b your-feature-branch`\n2. **Write code** with tests (100% coverage for new code)\n3. **Commit with DCO sign-off:**\n   ```bash\n   git commit -s -m \"component: description\"\n   # or auto-added by support/bootstrap hook\n   ```\n4. **Push to your fork** and open PR on GitHub\n\n### PR Title and Message Format\n\n**Title format:** `component: description` (lowercase)\n\nExamples:\n- `docs: fix grammar error`\n- `http conn man: add new feature`\n- `router: add x-envoy-overloaded header`\n- `tls: add support for TLS session ticket keys`\n\n**Commit message:**\n- Explain what changed and why\n- If fixing issue: `Fixes #XXX`\n- For behavioral changes: document before/after behavior\n- For deprecations: list what's deprecated\n\n**Use pull request template:** Automatically filled in when you open a PR\n- **Risk level:** Low | Medium | High\n- **Testing:** Describe testing performed\n- **Documentation:** Link to docs/release notes changes\n- **Release notes:** Update `changelogs/current.yaml` for user-facing changes\n- **API changes:** Reference [API Review Checklist](api/review_checklist.md)\n\n### DCO Sign-Off\n\nAll commits must be signed off with Developer Certificate of Origin:\n\n```bash\ngit commit -s  # Adds: Signed-off-by: Your Name <your.email@example.com>\n```\n\nAuto-signup via git alias:\n```bash\ngit config --add alias.c \"commit -s\"\n```\n\n**Fix DCO errors on existing PR:**\n```bash\ngit rebase -i HEAD~N  # Squash commits\ngit commit -s --amend  # Add sign-off\ngit push origin -f  # Force push (acceptable only for DCO fixes)\n```\n\n### PR Review Requirements\n\n- **Tests must pass** — No PRs merge with failing tests\n- **100% code coverage** — All new code must be covered by tests (or justified)\n- **Cross-company reviews** — For new extensions: at least one approver from a different organization than the author\n- **Senior maintainer review** — Core code requires senior maintainer approval\n- **Domain expert review** — Code should be reviewed by area expert (not necessarily maintainer)\n\n**Maintainers and reviewers:** See `OWNERS.md` for area experts\n\n### Coding Standards\n\n**Format:** Automatically enforced via clang-format\n- Line limit: 100 characters\n- Run fixes: `bazel run //tools/code_format:check_format -- fix`\n\n**Style:** [Google C++ style guide](https://google.github.io/styleguide/cppguide.html) with Envoy deviations:\n- Function names: camelCase starting lowercase (e.g., `doFoo()`)\n- Member variables: trailing underscore (e.g., `foo_`)\n- Enum values: PascalCase (e.g., `RoundRobin`)\n- Smart pointers: type aliased (e.g., `using FooPtr = std::unique_ptr<Foo>;`)\n- `#pragma once` for header guards\n- Code inside `Envoy` namespace\n- Anonymous namespaces preferred over `static`\n- Inclusive language policy: no \"whitelist\"/\"blacklist\"/\"master\"/\"slave\" terms\n\n**Linting:** clang-tidy (error-level enforced)\n\n**Inclusive language:**\n- ❌ \"whitelist\" → ✅ \"allowlist\"\n- ❌ \"blacklist\" → ✅ \"denylist\"/\"blocklist\"\n- ❌ \"master\" → ✅ \"primary\"/\"main\"\n- ❌ \"slave\" → ✅ \"secondary\"/\"replica\"\n\n### Important PR Guidelines\n\n- **Don't rebase after review starts** — GitHub forces reviewers to re-review everything\n- Use merge to pull main changes:\n  ```bash\n  git checkout main && git pull && git checkout your-branch && git merge main\n  ```\n- **Format checks:** Run pre-push checks locally via `./support/bootstrap`\n- **Don't use `--no-verify`** for hooks unless absolutely necessary (bypasses critical checks)\n- **Stale PRs:** PRs with >7 days of inactivity may be closed; can be reopened\n- **Pro-actively work on PR** — Don't abandon after opening\n- **Don't force push** after review starts (exception: DCO sign-off fixes)\n\n### PR Review Timeline\n\n- **Expected response:** Within one business day\n- **Senior maintainer:** Reviews all core code changes\n- **Domain experts:** Should review relevant areas (may not be maintainers)\n- **Anyone can review:** Community reviews welcome\n\n### Merging\n\n**Before merge:**\n1. All tests pass\n2. Coverage ≥100% for new code\n3. All documentation updated\n4. Release notes added (if user-facing)\n5. PR title/body cleaned up by maintainer\n\n**After merge:**\n- If PR has deprecations: notification sent to `envoy-announce@`\n- Squash merge used (commit history cleaned)\n- Maintainer ensures final commit message is correct\n\n### Runtime Guarding (High-Risk Changes)\n\nSome changes (major refactors, behavioral changes to HTTP processing) require runtime guards:\n\n```cpp\nif (Runtime::runtimeFeatureEnabled(\"envoy.reloadable_features.my_feature_name\")) {\n  [new code path]\n} else {\n  [old_code_path]\n}\n```\n\n- Both paths must have 100% coverage\n- May be enabled by default or after testing period\n- See: `source/common/runtime/runtime_features.cc`\n- Reference: `CONTRIBUTING.md` \"Runtime Guarding\" section\n\n## 6. Developer Workflow Example\n\n### Scenario: Fix bug in HTTP Connection Manager filter\n\n**Step 1: Discuss with community**\n```\n1. Search existing issues: Is this already tracked?\n2. If not, open GitHub issue: \"HTTP Connection Manager: [description of bug]\"\n3. Wait for confirmation from maintainers that it's not in progress\n```\n\n**Step 2: Set up development environment**\n```bash\n# Clone and setup\ngit clone https://github.com/YOUR_USERNAME/envoy.git\ncd envoy\n./support/bootstrap\n\n# Create feature branch\ngit checkout -b fix/http-conn-man-bug\n```\n\n**Step 3: Understand the codebase**\n```bash\n# HTTP Connection Manager code locations:\n# - Core: source/common/http/conn_manager_impl.cc/h\n# - Tests: test/common/http/conn_manager_impl_test.cc\n# - Integration: test/integration/ (various HTTP tests)\n\n# Search for references:\ngrep -r \"conn_manager_impl\" source/\n```\n\n**Step 4: Write tests first**\n```bash\n# Add failing test to test/common/http/conn_manager_impl_test.cc\n# Build and verify it fails\n./ci/run_envoy_docker.sh './ci/do_ci.sh dev //test/common/http:conn_manager_impl_test'\n```\n\n**Step 5: Implement the fix**\n```bash\n# Edit source/common/http/conn_manager_impl.cc\n# Follow style guide and coding standards\n```\n\n**Step 6: Run full test suite locally**\n```bash\n# Run all HTTP-related tests\n./ci/run_envoy_docker.sh './ci/do_ci.sh dev //test/common/http/...'\n\n# Run with sanitizers\n./ci/run_envoy_docker.sh './ci/do_ci.sh asan'\n\n# Check code formatting\nbazel run //tools/code_format:check_format -- fix\n```\n\n**Step 7: Commit and push**\n```bash\n# Commit with DCO sign-off\ngit add source/common/http/conn_manager_impl.{cc,h} test/common/http/conn_manager_impl_test.cc\ngit commit -s -m \"http conn man: fix [specific issue]\n\nFixes #ISSUE_NUMBER\n\nThis commit fixes the HTTP connection manager by [explanation of fix].\nThe bug occurred when [reproduction steps]. This is now fixed by\n[explanation of solution].\"\n\n# Push to fork\ngit push origin fix/http-conn-man-bug\n```\n\n**Step 8: Open PR on GitHub**\n```\n1. Go to: https://github.com/envoyproxy/envoy/compare/main...YOUR_USERNAME:fix/http-conn-man-bug\n2. Fill in PR template:\n   - Title: \"http conn man: fix [issue]\"\n   - Risk: Low (if small fix) | Medium (if moderate) | High (if major)\n   - Testing: \"Added unit test in test/common/http/conn_manager_impl_test.cc\"\n   - Documentation: \"N/A\" or link to docs changes\n   - Release notes: Add entry to changelogs/current.yaml\n   - Issues: \"Fixes #ISSUE_NUMBER\"\n3. Submit PR\n```\n\n**Step 9: Wait for CI and review**\n```\n1. Azure Pipelines runs (1-2 hours):\n   - Builds on Linux (Ubuntu, CentOS)\n   - macOS build\n   - All tests run\n   - Coverage checked\n   - Code formatting verified\n2. Maintainers and domain experts review\n3. Address feedback (new commits, don't rebase)\n```\n\n**Step 10: Merge**\n```\n1. All tests pass ✓\n2. All reviews approved ✓\n3. Maintainer merges with squash\n4. Your fix is in main!\n5. Celebrate! 🎉\n```\n\n### Key Commands Cheat Sheet\n\n```bash\n# Setup\ngit clone https://github.com/YOUR_USERNAME/envoy.git && cd envoy\n./support/bootstrap\n\n# Development\ngit checkout -b feature-name\n\n# Build and test (Docker)\n./ci/run_envoy_docker.sh './ci/do_ci.sh dev'\n./ci/run_envoy_docker.sh './ci/do_ci.sh dev //test/specific:test_target'\n./ci/run_envoy_docker.sh './ci/do_ci.sh asan'  # AddressSanitizer\n./ci/run_envoy_docker.sh './ci/do_ci.sh coverage'\n\n# Format\nbazel run //tools/code_format:check_format -- fix\n\n# Commit\ngit add [files]\ngit commit -s -m \"component: description\"\n\n# Push\ngit push origin feature-name\n\n# Rebase incoming changes (don't force push)\ngit checkout main && git pull\ngit checkout feature-name && git merge main\n\n# Rerun CI\n# (comment on PR): /retest\n# Or: git commit -s --allow-empty -m 'Kick CI' && git push\n```\n\n---\n\n## Additional Resources\n\n- **Build:** `bazel/README.md`\n- **Tests:** `test/README.md`, `test/integration/README.md`\n- **External dependencies:** `bazel/EXTERNAL_DEPS.md`\n- **Bazel rules guide:** `bazel/DEVELOPER.md`\n- **Extension policy:** `EXTENSION_POLICY.md`\n- **API versioning:** `api/API_VERSIONING.md`\n- **API review checklist:** `api/review_checklist.md`\n- **Repository layout:** `REPO_LAYOUT.md`\n- **Development toolchain:** `support/README.md`\n- **VS Code setup:** `tools/vscode/README.md`\n\n## Community\n\n- **Slack:** https://envoyproxy.slack.com/ (for quick questions)\n- **Mailing lists:** envoy-dev@, envoy-users@, envoy-announce@ (for announcements)\n- **Community meeting:** Bi-weekly on Tuesdays at 9am PT (see public [calendar](https://goo.gl/PkDijT))\n- **Code of conduct:** `CODE_OF_CONDUCT.md`\n","structuredPatch":[],"originalFile":null}}
